Current Commentary

Current Commentary

Preventing Floods

Yun

According to recent news, the Yangtze River water level has suddenly surged again. The capital Xiaguan has risen sharply by two and a half feet on the 10th. Wuhan has reached 40 feet, exceeding the water level during the great flood of twenty years ago. The area of Edong Chun has broken through 48 dikes, and more than 100,000 mu of farmland have been flooded. The disaster has already formed. I am panicked, but the counties have telegraphed the Hubei Provincial Government to allocate funds to help the emergency rescue project. The Hubei Provincial Government and the National Economic Committee and the Jianghan Engineering Bureau have not yet heard of a plan. I think of the tragic situation of the national flood twenty years ago, and I am frightened by the future dangers.

The total number of people affected by the national flood twenty years ago was about 25.2 million, which is equal to the total number of farmers in the United States. The area of affected arable land was about 87 million mu, accounting for about 56% of the total area of arable land in the country. The total amount of losses reached 200,000 million yuan, and the direct losses of damaged dikes and roads and other indirect losses are even inestimable. If I close my eyes and think quietly, the tragic scene of the land subsidence two years ago is vividly presented in front of me. The facts show that the disaster-stricken land has not been restored to this day, and many orphans and widows have been displaced. After this disaster, the national vitality was exhausted. How can this kind of tragic and inhumane disaster be repeated? The past is not far away, and our authorities should make preparations for the prevention of water dikes along the river.

Even more so, in today's civilized countries, most of them can prevent all disasters with human power, but in our country, there is no year without disasters for more than 20 years. Water, drought, locust, and hail disasters are all available. We don't know how to prevent them beforehand, and we can't remedy them afterwards. The whole country is in the persecution of disasters. This kind of phenomenon is seen in the civilized world of the 20th century, which cannot be said to be a great shame for the Chinese nation.

I believe that it is now imperative to urgently rescue the impending disaster in the Yangtze River Basin and actively prevent it from expanding. The National Government should strictly order the relevant authorities to step up the work of dikes and make preparations for the rainy day with great attention, so as to avoid seeing the disaster of two years ago today. It is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep is lost. Our authorities should pay attention to it.

Japan's Future Policies

Consolidating Asian and African Diplomatic Power

Adding Embassies and Consulates, Especially Focusing on China and India

The Military Budget is Increased, and the Ambition of Militarism is Not Checked

The Tokyo Ministry of Foreign Affairs has now adopted the following policies for the budget of the next fiscal year: ⑴ Because Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, it must consolidate Japan's economic and diplomatic power. ⑵ Reduce the number of embassies and consulates in Europe, and add embassies or consulates in Egypt, South Africa, the Near East, India, the South Seas, "Manchukuo," China, and Africa. ⑶ Pay special attention to the economic relations between Japan and India, and establish consulates in Karachi and Madras, and select one of the ambassadors as the consul general in Calcutta, so as to have equal power to discuss everything with the Governor-General of India. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

The two directors of the Tokyo Ministry of Foreign Affairs relied on the military's loudspeaker and suppressed the great ambassadors stationed abroad by taking advantage of the military's power, so they were attacked by the great ambassadors. Shiratori, the director of the Information Department, has been transferred to the Swedish ambassador, and Tani, the director of the Asian Affairs Department, still has no destination. It is heard that the army has recommended Tani Masayuki to be the councilor of the Japanese Embassy in Manchukuo, to be the supreme emperor of the pseudo-Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The official decision will be made within the next day. The successor to the director will recommend Yano, the counselor of the Japanese Embassy in China. Yano is the son-in-law of Ishii Kikujiro (the current Japanese representative to the World Economic Conference), a senior diplomat in Japan, and a brother of the previous Director of Information Shiratori Toshio. (12th China Alliance Dispatch)

When the Japanese Navy compiled its next fiscal year's budget, it had a so-called second naval replenishment plan. This matter is now attracting much attention. According to this plan, Japan will use 370,000,000 yuan to build more than 20 warships around 1936, including one 8,000-ton aircraft carrier, two 8,500-ton six-inch-diameter gun cruisers, seven 1,400-ton destroyers, one 5,000-ton mine-laying ship, twelve submarines of various tonnages, and several minesweepers. The naval authorities will formally discuss their budget plan after the government decides its attitude towards this matter. It is heard that the next naval budget is about 400,000,000 yuan (12th Reuters Dispatch)

Although the Japanese next army budget has not been submitted for consideration, its total amount is between 440,000,000 and 450,000,000 yuan. Generally speaking, the Japanese army expenses will be larger than before, because in addition to the current expenses of 200,000,000 yuan and the Manchurian military expenses of 140,000,000 to 150,000,000 yuan, it is also necessary to raise 100,000,000 yuan for the expenses of supplementing military equipment. Everyone expects that if there are no unexpected events, the Manchurian military expenses are expected to be reduced, because it is heard that the so-called bandit suppression work has now been almost completely completed. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

Japanese Cotton Industry

Sponsors a Boycott of Indian Cotton

The Japanese Anti-British Atmosphere is Strong

The Cotton Industry and Textile Industry Federation of Tokyo issued a statement to fully support the motion of the Cotton Textile Industry Association to boycott Indian raw cotton, and said that if the UK insists on its anti-Japanese attitude and cancels the commercial treaty, Japan must boycott all British goods, wool, wheat, wood, machinery, and steel are all included. (12th Reuters Dispatch

Dr. Schiny Advocates

Recovery of Territory Movement

Germans Don't Forget the South Seas Mandated Islands

Dr. Frank Schiny (one of the former investigators for the League of Nations Manchurian Case) said in a speech at the 51st meeting of the German Colonial Society today that the new government has completed unification in all parts of German national life, especially for foreign policy, and he hopes that this unification can be extended to colonial issues. All Germans should stand on a battle line in the near future to support the colonial movement. Germany wants to recover its old colonies as part of Germany's demand for equal status. He hopes that the Hitler government will not only seek military equality but also seek colonial equality. (11th National Telegraph)

London Times

On Sino-American New Loans

The London Times reported that the United States is rumored to have provided China with loans to purchase American cotton and wheat. The result will increase the uneasiness of British holders of Chinese bonds, because if Chinese national taxes are used to pay off the new debts, while the old debts of the British are continuously ignored, the British will inevitably consider this unfavorable to them. The close and organized actions taken by the holders of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway bonds are noteworthy. It is especially important that this was initiated by a large group of local investors in the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, because local creditors have legal access to the administration of the railway that secures their bonds, while creditors outside of China obviously have no such access. Therefore, their accusations of waste have considerable weight. (12th, Reuters)

Visible to All

Opening of the World Economic Conference

Gathering the Talents of Sixty-Six Nations in One Hall

The Greatest Gathering Since the Paris Peace Conference

The British Monarch Delivers a Welcome Speech

Hoping to Heal the Economic Sickness Through Collective Efforts

Prime Minister MacDonald Delivers the Opening Address

Strongly Emphasizing the Need for International Cooperation to Avert the Crisis

Sixteen National Representatives Elected to Form the Steering Committee

General Debate to Begin at Ten O'Clock This Morning

London: This afternoon, the British monarch held the opening ceremony of the World Economic Conference at the Royal Geological Museum in South Kensington, with the aim of healing economic ills. The British monarch addressed the representatives of various countries from the golden throne on the conference podium, stating, "At this time of economic hardship sweeping the world, I welcome you to this country with a deep sense of responsibility. As the head of state hosting the opening meeting of an international conference, I believe this is an unprecedented event in history. I wish to express my satisfaction that this conference could be held, and I deeply believe that this joint effort can produce beneficial results. I welcome the representatives of the member states of the League of Nations. I have always followed the work of the League of Nations with keen admiration and attention. The League of Nations convened this conference and prepared everything with the valuable services of expert committees. Without the League of Nations, without the ideals of the League of Nations, I cannot but doubt whether this conference could be held. I also warmly welcome the representatives of non-League of Nations member states. I acknowledge their willingness to join in a spirit of beneficial cooperation in joint discussions. Finally, I would like to extend a special welcome to the representatives of the British Dominions and India." At this point, the British monarch switched to French and continued, "As I look around at this solemn gathering, my heart is moved very deeply. This gathering may seem great, but what it represents is an infinitely greater concept of hope and aspirations for the entire world. The world is now in a precarious state, and your responsibilities are extremely heavy. Unless you proceed with goodwill and sincere cooperation, it will be difficult to achieve success. I extend my hand to you and sincerely wish that your efforts will produce the pleasant results that the world urgently awaits." At this point, the British monarch switched back to English and said, "I fully acknowledge the difficulty of the conference's work, but the genuine desire to reach an agreement is firmly and demonstrably present. This gives me great hope. All countries in the world share the same ailments. This is evident from the increase in the number of unemployed people. In terms of human suffering, I have often cited these figures as a cause for concern in recent years, and they are also a cause for concern for everyone gathered here today who bears the heavy responsibility of government. In this universally recognized crisis, I urge you to cooperate to seek the ultimate happiness of the world, utilizing the great power of the world to safeguard the material progress of civilization. This is certainly not beyond human reach. The world's power has not diminished, but inventions and organizations are emerging one after another, increasing possibilities to the extent that abundant production has created new and difficult problems. Accompanying this astonishing material progress is a new recognition of the value of countries supporting and cooperating with each other. Today is truly an opportunity to contribute a new conscience of shared interests to serve humanity. I now declare this conference open with the firm belief that mutual consultation is the first step towards righteous action. I will follow the discussions of this conference with the utmost interest and attention. I earnestly pray that the efforts of your work will restore the world to a path of prosperity and orderly progress." (12th, Reuters)

London: After the British monarch left the conference hall, Chairman MacDonald immediately delivered the opening address, stating that all countries are suffering from a common ailment, as can be clearly seen from the daily increase in the number of unemployed people. Since 1929, prices have fallen far below the cost of production and have fluctuated erratically, disrupting the normal relationships of all economic activities. Coupled with the restrictions on trade, the widespread crisis has increased. Tariffs and exchange controls have reduced international trade by half in one or two years. The large number of countries abandoning the gold standard is unprecedented in peacetime since the establishment of an international medium of exchange. MacDonald then discussed war debts, solemnly stating that before the obstacles to economic recovery are removed, we must resolve the war debts, complete the work of the Lausanne Conference, and solve this troublesome problem once and for all in light of the current state of the world. He then strongly emphasized that the World Economic Conference is the result of the Lausanne Conference. He recalled that after the Lausanne Conference completed its urgent work, it declared that in order to clear the world crisis, a conference with a wider scope should be held. At that time, this intention was recorded. He further elaborated on the necessity of international cooperation between countries, saying that no country can permanently benefit itself by sacrificing others, and that mutual benefit is a necessary condition for seeking individual benefits. (12th, National Telegram)

London: After MacDonald delivered the opening address and the report of the Credentials Committee was approved at the World Economic Conference, China, Argentina, Czechoslovakia, France, Germany, Great Britain, Hungary, Italy, Japan, Mexico, the Netherlands, Spain, Sweden, the United States, Russia, and Canada were elected to the Steering Committee. MacDonald announced that the general debate would begin at 10:30 tomorrow morning and adjourned the meeting at 4:39 p.m. The Steering Committee then immediately convened a closed meeting (12th, National Telegram)

Clearly Audible in Tokyo

Tokyo: The wireless broadcast of the speech delivered by the British monarch at the opening of the World Economic Conference was received here in Tokyo tonight and was very clear. However, the speech by British Prime Minister MacDonald was largely unintelligible. (12th, Reuters)

Yan and Koo Arrive Early

London: This afternoon, Dr. Yan Huiquing and Dr. Koo Vi Kyuin arrived at the opening ceremony of the World Economic Conference quite early, so they sat in the front row facing the British monarch's podium. The staff who handled the historical translation work for the Sino-Japanese disputes in the past were all present today, making the gathering feel even more like a conference in Geneva. (12th, Reuters)

Students Make Strange Noises

London: The British monarch departed from Windsor Palace at 2:07 p.m. today, traveled by car to London, and arrived at the venue at 2:50 p.m. There were no demonstrations encountered along the way, but just two minutes after arriving at the venue, a group of students from the Royal College of Science, located across the street from the venue, made catcalls (expressing ridicule, commonly seen in theaters) repeatedly. The police quickly intervened, and the noise subsided. The police called these students' strange actions "the boiling of youthful spirits." Unexpectedly, just two minutes after the British monarch took the stage to speak, there was renewed clamor from the demonstrators, and the sound of machine guns rang out from the thoroughfare, continuing until the end of the monarch's speech. This is a strange phenomenon rarely seen in Britain. (12th, National Telegram)

London: The World Economic Conference, which is of great historical value, has been fully prepared and will open at 3:00 p.m. today. The representatives of sixty-six countries have all arrived in England.

A Gathering of Talents: Among them are one head of state (the President of Switzerland, M. Etter), eight prime ministers or premiers, twenty foreign ministers, and forty-seven other cabinet members. It can truly be called the largest gathering of politicians and economists since the Versailles Peace Conference.

Venue Arrangement: The venue is the Royal Geological Museum in South Kensington, London. It is magnificent and unparalleled. The seating in the venue was not completed until a few hours before the opening. In front of the splendid podium are the seats for the representatives of the sixty-six countries, with seats for advisors, the diplomatic corps, journalists, and special guests arranged on three sides. Seats for ordinary listeners and guests are on both sides and at the rear of the conference hall.

Representative Seating: There are fourteen rows of representative seats. Those with more representatives generally sit in the front rows. England and France each have eight representatives, so they sit in the front row. The United States, Germany, Italy, and Japan each have six representatives, sitting in the second row. China has three representatives, sitting in the third row. Although Soviet Russia has only two representatives, several seats are specially reserved for advisors to sit with them, because Soviet Russia has a special relationship in the world economy. There are 152 seats for the diplomatic corps, 144 seats for economic experts and advisors, and 45 seats for special guests, all specially invited guests to the opening ceremony. Three hundred journalists representing participating countries also occupy a corner close to the podium.

A Glimpse of the Opening: After 2:30 p.m. today, the representatives entered the venue in succession. The sound of welcome from the audience was like thunder. The opening was announced at 3:00 p.m. The British monarch personally delivered a

Page 8

(8)

welcome speech, which was then broadcast worldwide via radio. This was followed by the opening address by British Prime Minister MacDonald. Because today's meeting was an opening ceremony, only organizational matters were considered.

Conference Procedure: Formal business will begin on Tuesday, when the chief representatives of each country will present their economic recovery plans in turn. According to Chairman MacDonald's intention, each person's speech is limited to ten minutes. After that, group committee meetings will be held. After some committees reach important agreements, a plenary session will be held. As for the agenda, there has been little discussion in the past two days. Most of the representatives are engaged in formal visits with each other. (12th, National News Agency)

Tzai-Sung Meets MacDonald

Freely Discussing Sino-British Relations

London: Chinese Finance Minister T.V. Soong went to the Prime Minister's residence today to have a long and earnest conversation with MacDonald. At that time, Sino-British relations and the situation in the Far East were discussed. Soong spent most of his time today at the Prime Minister's residence, and returned to London in the evening. He dined with Sir Esher. (11th, Reuters)

Economic Non-Aggression Treaty

Russian Representative Plans to Propose to the Conference

London: It is rumored that Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov intends to propose, in the name of the Soviet government, to convene a conference to negotiate an economic non-aggression treaty. (11th, Havas)

Moscow: Today, Moscow newspapers predict that there will be an attempt to consolidate an anti-Russian bloc under British leadership at the World Economic Conference. The Communist Party organ Izvestia advises the world to consider whether it would be more beneficial to enjoy peaceful trade relations and normal credit with Soviet Russia than to attempt to rejuvenate itself with the blood of Soviet Russia. (12th, National Electric)

Japan's Challenging Attitude

Focusing on Eliminating Boycotts

Avoiding Discussion of the Sino-Japanese Case

Tokyo: Before the opening of the World Economic Conference, Britain showed an undisguised challenging attitude towards the Japanese economy. Therefore, Japan's established policy for the Economic Conference has also become a belligerent attitude. Foreign Minister Uchida issued the following instructions to Representative Ishii: The Japanese government's attitude towards the Economic Conference is to cooperate with various countries in principle, but if there is anything that endangers Japan's existence, it will resolutely reject it. For example, regarding China's anti-Japanese boycott movement, Japan does not seek international assistance and handles it independently. Therefore, at the World Economic Conference, the Japanese representative will not make any demands regarding the Chinese anti-Japanese problem. Also, if a certain country participating in the conference oppresses the Japanese economy, Japan will also adopt an active policy to start an economic dispute with it. (11th, Japan United Electric)

Tokyo: It is now known that the Japanese government has not issued new instructions to the Japanese delegation attending the World Economic Conference, because they had already received detailed instructions when the delegation left Tokyo. It is heard that the Japanese delegation will advocate free trade and the elimination of obstacles to free trade among nations in order to relieve the current global commercial oppression. As for the issue of economic boycotts, the Japanese representative will transfer the matter to Chief Representative Ishii for handling according to the situation. It is now heard that if other countries agree to conclude a general tariff agreement, Japan will also join, but Japanese officials say that Japan has not increased taxes for ten years, so the tax rate is lower. (11th, Reuters)

London: The Japanese delegation held its first delegation meeting at 5:00 a.m. on the 11th to discuss countermeasures for the Economic Conference. Plenipotentiary Ishii, along with Deputy Representatives Matsudaira and Fukai and other key members, attended. First, the content of Representative Ishii's speech at the conference on the 14th was decided. As a result of exchanging opinions on the method of selecting members of the Economic Conference Steering Committee, if the chairman appoints the committee members, Representative Ishii of Japan will naturally be a member, and it is even possible that he may obtain the position of vice-chairman. As for the general committee, the currency committee, and the economic committee and other subcommittees, Japan will decide on representatives after they are established. According to the current situation, Japan intends not to propose the Sino-Japanese issue, but if it is proposed, it is determined to resist resolutely. (11th, Japan United Electric)

Japanese Goods Dumped Abroad

Causing Sleepless Nights for Various Countries

Berlin: The Kolonia Newspaper published an article on the London Conference, saying, "The London Conference wants to stabilize currencies and give them a sound basis, but it may encounter an obstacle, that is, Japan is competing with people in the world market with its currency inflation policy." The newspaper said that Japan's competition is causing sleepless nights for export merchants in various countries. It said, "Japan is militaristic and forgets its reasons. It wants to use currency inflation policy as a financial talisman, and does not have time to think about the irremediable consequences in the future. The United States does not want to recognize the position Japan has obtained in China through aggressive means, so it is absolutely impossible to make political concessions to Japan. So, is it possible to find a way economically to avoid resistance from Japan? But it is not necessarily possible, because the principle of most-favored-nation treatment has become shaky since the Ottawa Agreement was established." (11th, Havas)

Two Major Difficulties at Present

Currency and War Debts

Paris Times Commentary on the World Economic Conference: Before the opening of the conference, we feel that there are two issues that greatly affect the progress of the conference's work. One is the currency issue, which cannot be sincerely resolved without restoring the gold standard. But as of now, the US dollar and the British pound have shown no signs of stability. The currency issue can never be resolved by forcibly redistributing gold by human power. If this kind of perfunctory method is adopted, the currencies of various countries will be generally devalued. Trying this kind of method in the current state of world economic chaos is inevitably dangerous. All countries in the world that do not want to live in a state of spiritual and financial chaos resolutely oppose this perfunctory policy. In addition to currency, the second important issue is the resolution of war debts. (11th, Havas)

Three-Nation Financial Conference

Opinions on Stabilizing Currency Prices Tend to Converge

Paris: Paris newspapers today published news of the British, American, and French financial officials' meeting held in London yesterday in great detail. According to reports, the discussion centered on currency consolidation and other currency issues. However, the Petit Parisien newspaper claimed that the purpose of the meeting was to discuss a number of outstanding issues and to reach a solution before the opening of the World Economic Conference so that they could be jointly presented at the World Economic Conference. These three countries now control 70% of the world's total amount of money, so it is imperative to exchange opinions beforehand. Other newspapers, such as Le Matin, claimed that regarding the stabilization of the monetary system, an agreement has been approached by this meeting, but the complete agreement itself has not yet arrived. (11th, National Electric)

War Debt Repayment Issue

White House Studies Whether It Is Legal

US Congress to Adjourn Today or Tomorrow

Washington: President Roosevelt's staff is now studying whether partial repayment of war debts is legal, and whether accepting such repayment would constitute a clear recognition that the remaining debts can be unpaid. It is heard that Britain has already made an informal proposal to the US government through its ambassador to the United States, Lindsay, to repay part of the war debt due on June 15. The Baltimore Sun editorial said that partial repayment would create political disputes, as the move would be based on the Lausanne Convention. (11th, Reuters)

Washington: Congressional Democratic leaders met with President Roosevelt today and stated to the President that Congress could adjourn tonight or tomorrow. The President's decision on the June debt, such as approving partial repayment, will be welcomed by those who oppose the cancellation of war debts. (12th, Reuters)

Some Diplomat

Impressions of the Conference

Beijing: According to a diplomat, the sole purpose of this World Economic Conference is to solve the world economic problem, but because the inside story is too complicated, the result is still difficult to determine at present. However, judging from the various conferences in the past, it is expected that the outcome of this conference will be difficult to be optimistic about. Our country's participation in this conference is not holding great hope, but is regarded as a ray of light for resolving disputes. Whether or not a good result can be obtained in the future depends entirely on whether the great powers have sincerity. It is heard that if this conference proceeds smoothly, in addition to discussing the six major items stipulated, other issues may also be discussed. In short, I hope that the people of the country will not have too high hopes for this conference, and even if there is a good resolution, it may not be implemented. The resolutions of the League of Nations in the past can serve as a clear lesson. In this serious situation, we must rely on our own efforts to escape the oppression of force. (12th, Central News Agency)

Central Government Plans to Raise 20 Million Yuan

To Relieve the North China War Zone

The Government and the Banking Sector Will Each Raise 10 Million Yuan

Loan to Farmers in the Same Way as the International Famine Relief Commission Last Year

Nanjing: A certain central committee member said that the central government's method of relieving the North China war zone will refer to the method undertaken by the China International Famine Relief Commission last year in Jiangxi and Anhui provinces. It will start from the counties along the Great Wall and gradually move inward. The relief funds are planned to be raised by the government and the banking sector, each raising 10 million yuan, and will be loaned to farmers in combination. For every two yuan borrowed, one yuan will be repaid. Interest will be calculated at an annual rate of four percent on the amount borrowed. This fund is being planned by the government. At the same time, another 1 million yuan will be raised specifically for office use. In the future, special commissioners will be sent to take charge, and a committee of an advisory nature will be established to assist. The goal is to complete it within one year. In order to maintain the discipline of the troops stationed in the war zone, the government will pay attention to the supplies for the troops, and will also form a special gendarmerie to maintain order. This type of gendarmerie will be under the command of the special commissioner, and the work area will be limited to the counties north of the Beining Line, east of Tanggu and Peiping, east and north of the Peisui Line's Peiping and Kalgan, south of the Great Wall, Shanhaiguan, and Kalgan, and north of the coast, Shanhaiguan, and Dagu. (12th, Special Telegram)

Central Party Headquarters and National Government

Two Memorial Week Reports

Chen Guofu: Importance of Improving Traditional Chinese Medicine

Shao Yuanchong: National Survival and Revival

Nanjing: The Central Committee held its 82nd Memorial Week at 8:00 a.m. on the 12th, attended by Ye Chucang, Wang Qi, Li Ciwen, Xiao Zhongzhen, Chen Guofu, Zheng Zhannan, Li Jingzhai, Hong Ludong,

Chen Lifu, Ju Zheng, etc. Ye Chucang chaired the meeting, and Chen Guofu reported on "The Importance of Improving Traditional Chinese Medicine," stating that Chinese medicine has a history of about several thousand years, but because it does not know how to improve, there is no progress, which has led to the promotion of Western medicine, and traditional Chinese medicine is not valued. Germany and Japan have the most developed medicine, but they still take the advantages of our Chinese medicine. We should not discriminate against it. Moreover, people in the mainland still rely on Chinese medicine when they are sick because it is widespread and the cost is small, and because Chinese medicine is suitable for the constitution of Chinese people. Therefore, improving and promoting Chinese medicine is essential. The way to improve is to explain or apply the principles of Chinese medicine using scientific methods, and to establish Chinese medicine schools to improve the talents of Chinese medicine practitioners. Domestic scientists should also help the development of Chinese medicine, improve its diagnostic methods and chemical refining of the components of Chinese medicine, and preserve its inherent strengths, so as to seek happiness for the majority of people in the mainland. I hope everyone will pay attention to and promote it. The meeting adjourned at 9:00 a.m. (12th, Central News Agency)

Nanjing: The National Government held the Premier's Memorial Week at 9:00 a.m. on the 12th, attended by Chairman Lin, Shao Yuanchong, Chen Shaokuan, Wang Yongbin, Zhu Jiaju, Lin Xiang, Lu Chao, Zhou Yawei, and more than 400 civil and military officials. Chairman Lin led the ceremony, followed by Shao Yuanchong's report entitled "National Survival and National Revival," based on the Premier's doctrine of nationalism. He described the foundation of national survival and the path to national revival, hoping that the people of the country would do their best in their spirit and time, follow the Premier's doctrine, seek national survival, and achieve national revival. His detailed explanations moved the audience. (12th, Central News Agency)

Unemployed Overseas Chinese in Nagasaki

Measures for Returning to China Agreed Upon

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission in Nanjing consulted on measures to transport unemployed overseas Chinese in Nagasaki back to China. The result was that there were only 270 unemployed overseas Chinese in that area, including 184 from Fujian and only 3 from Shandong. Since the number was not large, it was inconvenient to send a special ship to pick them up. They should still take ordinary ships back to China. After arriving in China, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Ministry of Railways would reduce or waive ship and train fares to return them to their hometowns. The necessary expenses will be jointly submitted to the Executive Yuan to request the Ministry of Finance to allocate funds. (12th Dispatch)

Red Bandits in Sichuan

Tian and Liu Strive to Suppress

Xie Tianmin, a representative of Tian Songyao in Nanjing, told people that after Bazhong fell, Tian Songyao and Liu Cunhou were striving to encircle and suppress the Red bandits in Sichuan. Yongding River Rises Sharply

Hailstorms Cause Disaster in Shanxi Province

Taiyuan Also Suffers from Floods

At around 4 PM on the 10th, Taiyuan suddenly experienced a hailstorm with hailstones as large as eggs, lasting for about half an hour, followed by heavy rain. The streets became canals, and flash floods broke out in the mountains east of the city, breaching the banks of the Jian and Sha rivers. The water rose more than twenty feet, inundating countless fields and washing away dozens of people, killing more than twenty. The northeast, west, and south sides of the city became a watery expanse. The police and soldiers urgently closed the southwest three city gates. The water did not flood the city. By noon on the 11th, the water level had begun to recede slightly. The power lines between Pingyao and Taiyuan were destroyed by the wind, and there were no reports for two days. (11th Dispatch)

Hailstorms struck most of the counties in northern and southern Shanxi on the 10th. The larger hailstones were the size of bowls, severely damaging crops. It was the worst hailstorm in decades. According to a telegram from Changzhi County, hailstorms occurred at noon on the 10th, accumulating two inches of ice in a short time, wiping out all the green seedlings. Spring wheat was particularly badly damaged in the Hedong area. (12th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The hailstorm disaster near Taiyuan, the provincial capital of Shanxi, is extremely severe. Refugees are flocking in, and many have already died due to lack of food and clothing. Various counties have sent telegrams to the provincial government to report the disaster. (12th Dispatch)

It is necessary to collect the full price for passenger and freight transport in order to maintain it. It has been decided that after the railway opens, all preferential travel passes and the practice of attaching cars will not apply. Austrian Political Assassination Case

A National Telegram from Vienna on the 12th: Two prominent Austrian politicians were assassinated on Sunday: Dr. Rentran, a former cabinet member, and Dr. Sataider, Governor of Tyrol. Rentran was not injured, while Dr. Shi was shot. After the two cases occurred, the people were shaken and the authorities were on high alert. According to unconfirmed news from official and private sources, a murder occurred at the Innsbruck National Socialist Party headquarters, which was occupied by the police last night, and everyone inside was arrested. It is expected that the leaders of the Innsbruck National Socialist Party will be arrested within a few days. Dr. Shi, who was in Tyrol inspecting the new auxiliary police, was returning by car. Just after getting out of the car, someone in a car coming from the opposite direction fired seven shots at him. The doctor was hit in the elbow and his bones were shattered. The murderer escaped without a trace. Dr. Rentran was traveling by car to a small town when a truck suddenly blocked the road. The driver urgently turned the machine and stopped, and at this time, two bombs exploded a few yards away. The doctor was unharmed, and the murderer also escaped. It is reported that the Self-Defense Force in Krim Earth, Lower Austria, searched the local National Socialist Party headquarters and the two sides fought.

Exchanged Important Opinions on Military Affairs and Immigration

The President of Seiyukai Will Find Ways to Resolve Internal Disputes

He left at 11:00 AM. The policy for the relocation of divisions will be decided in 1934 and implemented in 1935. There is no need to increase troops for border defense. Korean immigration will be implemented under the army's control starting in 1933. The issue of unification was not discussed.

It is reported that Suzuki is scheduled to declare his decision at the cadre meeting on the 14th, and the content of his countermeasures is said to be the following three items: 1) Acknowledging that the current cabinet is incapable of undertaking Japanese politics in times of emergency. 2) Standing on a free position in the future, monitoring the government's facilities from a national and policy-based perspective, affirming what is right and criticizing what is wrong. 3) Not immediately withdrawing cabinet members from the Seiyukai, but waiting until a policy conflict occurs with the government in the future before withdrawing its cabinet members to ease the demands of the self-respect faction.

Feng Yuxiang in the Northwest Corner

National Security

Starting from the Beginning

Since General Christ was forced to retreat on the Longhai Line in the 19th year of the Republic of China, he has been depressed. He has been lurking in half the sky in the Northwest, reading and writing. After the September 18th Incident, General Christ began to shout the slogan of "Resistance" just like everyone else. Although the voice was gentle and pleasant, General Christ still did not run to the front line. But this time it has changed. General Christ, who was squatting in the library in Tu'ergou, Zhangjiakou, could no longer bear the sound of the Luan East artillery fire. General Christ stood on the top of Tu'ergou, Zhangjiakou, and shouted, and actually implemented the anti-Japanese war. So, the war clouds in the northwest corner gradually appeared tense in the newspapers. Anyway, people who don't live in the northwest corner, who can know what is going on? However, the newspaper said, "The Japanese and puppet troops occupied Guyuan and approached Zhangjiakou. Fang Zhenwu fought a great battle with the rebel army in Dushikou..." What is this if it is not true resistance to Japan?

I lived in "Zhangjiakou," the provincial capital of Chahar Province, for more than a month, and also had a face-to-face meeting with General Christ. At the same time, on the day when General Christ automatically took over the position of Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces in the library in Tu'ergou, Zhangjiakou, (May 26) I was still living in the Huayuan Hotel in Zhangjiakou, and I was fortunate enough to attend such a great ceremony of anti-Japanese war. Even the heavens seemed to be helping General Christ, and at 4 o'clock in the afternoon, there was a heavy rain. I read the great announcement of the Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces in the rain, and fled Zhangjiakou in the northwest corner in a mess on the 27th. Now, General Christ has truly contacted the Japanese and puppet troops. According to recent reports, the main battle between the two armies is about to begin. So, how can I not report to the readers in detail everything about General Christ's actions in Zhangjiakou? Finally, I must declare that this record is completely faithful and does not contain any emotionality. Besides, I used to be a small soldier, and I also have considerable admiration for General Christ.

㈠ Christ General in Tu'er Gou

Tu'er Gou is located south of Zhangjiakou Railway Station, and the library is situated in Tu'er Gou. It is said that before Christ General resided in the library, ordinary people could still enter to read books. However, since Christ General moved in, the security has become strict. To reach the library from the city, one must cross the railway, turn halfway to the right, make two forty-five-degree angle turns, and endure some sandy dust. When approaching the library by about three hundred meters in a quiet alley, one can see Christ General's guards. There are multiple sentry posts on the corners of the walls. Each guard holds a bright broadsword in his right hand and a wooden-handled hand grenade on his belt. Outside the library's earthen gate, there are also two guards, armed with broadswords and Mauser pistols. The faces of the guards are all dark and shiny. Here, we acknowledge that Christ General is a good example of how to train soldiers. One often sees Christ General's guards carrying large black coal chunks on their shoulders. At the same time, the air is always filled with the majestic and mournful tunes of military songs in the mornings and evenings.

It is said that since Christ General moved into the library, he has been constantly reading books. Unable to understand them himself, he has hired several teachers to instruct him from time to time. Christ General is confident in his ability to handle guns, having gained considerable expertise. Thus, he has started studying politics anew, including the Three Principles of the People. It goes without saying that Christ General is very familiar with Soviet communism, as well as fascism, which he has studied deeply. Therefore, his ultimate goal is to resist Japan. Although Duolun fell and Chahar East was in danger, Christ General did not express anything concrete. But this shot was fired correctly. At least the title of Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces can be worn. The library in Tu'er Gou has transformed into the headquarters of the Allied Forces. At this time, Zhangjiakou in the northwest corner has become Christ General's base for resisting Japan.

Not long ago, Christ General suffered from a sore throat. It just so happened that at that time, I took a rickshaw to visit him at the library in Tu'er Gou. After passing the gatekeeper's inspection, I presented a card and asked the dispatch office to forward it. Little did I know that they seemed surprised when they saw my card. A burly soldier next to me said to himself, "Ah! From Shanghai. Such a long way. Must be a Southerner." I pretended not to hear. The soldier wearing a blue Zhongshan suit who was delivering my message asked very casually as he turned back, "Sir, where are you from?" "Ah…," I paused slightly before saying, "I am from Henan." As a result, the gray-clad figures around me looked at me with even more surprise, muttering, "Ah, a Henan person."

I stood next to the guardhouse in front of the library for five minutes. The messenger in the blue Zhongshan suit came out from the second gate. I quickly greeted him, and he said very politely, "Sir, I am truly sorry. Mr. Feng's sore throat has not yet healed. I am truly sorry to have disappointed you. If you have anything, you can discuss it with Mr. Feng in writing." Hearing this, I still could not meet Mr. Feng. At the same time, I was asked to discuss things in writing, which was quite novel. After a long pause, I said to him in a sincere tone, "I am sorry to bother you. Please tell Mr. Feng again that I have come a long way from Shanghai. Furthermore, the people of the country are very concerned about Mr. Feng's current situation. We journalists are like representatives of those who are eager to know Mr. Feng's condition. Therefore, it is always better to have a few words in person. It is impossible for a journalist to visit an important person and only communicate in writing." The young soldier listened to my sharp but conciliatory words. He turned around and went back in for a long time. This time, it was still not successful, but the meaning had become somewhat flexible. "Sir, Mr. Feng, following the doctor's orders, really cannot meet with you. Please leave your address. This afternoon, around six or seven o'clock, Mr. Feng may send a representative to talk to you, and Mr. Feng will be responsible for what the representative says." Hearing the final answer, I knew that further entanglement would be useless. I gave them a polite bow with my hat off. They all widened their eyes and gave me a solemn and orderly salute. I got back into the rickshaw in the wind, sand, and dust, thinking to myself, "Ah, Mr. Feng's sore throat is probably because he shouted anti-Japanese slogans too enthusiastically."

After returning from the Tu'er Gou Library, I waited obediently for our Christ General's representative at the Huayuan Hotel. Right at six fifteen, the representative I was waiting for was led in by the waiter. This representative was very burly, wearing a small white American sailor-style hat, and had a very hearty demeanor. As soon as he entered, he said in a Luandong accent, "Are you Mr. Wan?" "Yes." "What is your surname?" I asked. "My surname is Zhang." At this time, he was already sitting in a chair by the window. I gave him a Fortress cigarette, and he lit it himself. I intended to exchange business cards with him, but he said politely, "I am sorry, sir, I do not have a business card with me. Let me write it for you." So he wrote three characters on my business card, "Zhang Jiurong." Immediately afterward, he said very seriously, "Today, Mr. Feng's throat is not well, so he asked me, a brother, to talk to you for a few words. But I have one thing I must state, which is that it is best not to publish my name in the newspaper." I nodded at the time. (Now it seems that I have lost my credibility. If Mr. Zhang, you see this piece of writing, I offer you twelve thousand apologies.) We were silent for about two minutes between us. I began to ask him, "Mr. Zhang, what are Mr. Feng's opinions on the current Sino-Japanese war? At the same time, when will Mr. Feng's method of resisting Japan be realized?" He rolled his eyes upward twice, opened his thick lips, and spoke in a very loud voice, as if giving a speech in front of a large crowd. He said to me, "Mr. Feng always feels that the biggest disadvantage is that we cannot fight the war with the entire nation united. The defeat of our army in Luandong was not a combat failure, but a failure of the overall strategy. The command cannot be unified, so the enemy's advance is even faster. As for Mr. Feng's anti-Japanese proposal, it cannot be realized. On this point, we must understand Mr. Feng's difficulties. He is not just shouting anti-Japanese slogans like others, but he has no opportunity to realize them." "Then what kind of view does Mr. Feng have on the future of Chahar Province?" He shook his head slightly, and a smile quickly flashed across his lips. At the same time, his speech-like voice became a little lower. "Chahar? Mr. Feng will preserve it no matter what. Mr. Feng has long said that he is willing to be shot to death by the Japanese artillery to fulfill his anti-Japanese wish. Sir, you watch, Mr. Feng will definitely be supported by the people in the near future." Supported by the people, what a resounding sentence. I listened quietly to his endless eloquent remarks. We talked for about an hour. Finally, I said to him again, "Mr. Zhang, it is best to find a way to have me talk to Mr. Feng for a few words." He pondered for a moment. "Okay, you listen to the phone." In this way, we, Christ General's representative, Mr. Zhang Jiurong, shook hands heartily with each other and said goodbye in the lamplight. (To be continued)

The Central Government Seeks a Political Solution to the Chahar Situation

The Problem of Reorganizing the Luandong Puppet Army is Under Negotiation

A special dispatch from Beiping: After the ceasefire agreement was established, the Japanese troops in the counties of Hebei Province mostly remained in their original defenses without withdrawing. Except for their baggage and artillery, which were transported away first, only a few infantry units moved. The puppet army in Luandong once requested to be reorganized by us. The authorities were quite hesitant about the handling method, believing that if the puppet army repented and sincerely returned, then their past could be forgiven and they could be given a new path. However, after being reorganized, they must be transferred to other places. At a minimum, the puppet army should be moved away from Luandong, retrained, and thoroughly reformed. As a result, the two sides had different opinions, and this issue was temporarily put on hold. Our side also prepared to resolve the issue of reorganization by force if necessary, but the proposal has now been abandoned. Meanwhile, Li Jichun, the leader of the puppet army, still repeatedly requested reorganization, but was firmly rejected by us. Later, after Li's repeated requests, expressing no other intention, the Hebei Provincial Government no longer insisted on rejecting the reorganization. However, the transfer and training must comply with our intentions, otherwise, other solutions should still be sought and no leniency would be shown. Li Jichun and his ilk's intentions are entirely for personal gain and have no established views. However, because the Japanese side does not want the puppet army to be transferred away from Luandong, they have secretly expressed opposition. Relying on their guidance, it is difficult to disobey. For a time, they did not want to give up the Luandong area immediately. This matter is currently under discussion, and there is no concrete solution yet. The puppet army near Yangzhuang in Ninghe, according to official announcements, has withdrawn to Sandaqiao. Japanese troops from Dongwo occasionally send scouts to the Yangzhuang area to reconnoiter. The Lutai area is quiet and unchanged. Regarding the opening of the Beining Railway between Pingyu, it will still take some time. The Railway Bureau, due to the delayed recovery of lost territory, has proposed to restore traffic ahead of schedule. If there are no safety problems in the future, a trial run can be started. However, it will be at least ten days later. East of Tongzhou, in the areas of Daxiao Dongzhuang northeast of the canal, the puppet army has not only not withdrawn but has continued to increase, buying off unemployed Hui people nearby to act as guides, and harassing villages from time to time, looting, raping, and doing whatever they please. In Xiji, the puppet army attacked and looted everything. The two largest wineries in the district, which is known for producing wine, suffered a total loss of fifty to sixty thousand yuan. The suburbs of Tongzhou are very peaceful. Most of the Japanese troops are concentrated in Sanhe. Many refugees have returned to their hometowns. The villages far east of Tongzhou, because they cannot bear the harassment of the puppet army, have all fled to Tongzhou to seek refuge with relatives and friends to escape temporarily. Even if the puppet army issue can be resolved smoothly in the future, banditry will still be inevitable. The future hidden worries still await the authorities to plan and find ways to eliminate them, so that the people can be safe. Therefore, all the follow-up work in North China is very important.

The Japanese Army Motegi Cavalry Brigade in Chahar East is now concentrated in Duolun. Liu Guitang's puppet army is mostly in Bao(chang) Kang(bao) and Guyuan. There are also many puppet troops in Guyuan. Since yesterday (9th), the puppet army has stopped advancing west, seemingly watching and waiting. The central government originally did not want to expand the Zhangyuan crisis, but since the Japanese and puppet armies have a tendency to actively covet Zhangbei, if Zhangjiakou falls into enemy hands, then Pingjin will be in a tense situation again. The future is very worrying. After repeated consultations by various parties, it was generally advocated to handle everything with peaceful means. It is heard that the military authorities have a proper plan for maintaining security in Chahar Province. In order to avoid disputes, the government has repeatedly telegraphed the Political Committee stationed in Pingjin to seek a solution quickly. Huang Fu has been carrying out disposal matters with He Yingqin and other dignitaries, proceeding with seven parts political power and three parts military power at the same time. Regarding Feng Yuxiang's personal whereabouts, they are doing their best to use political methods to promote unity. Regarding the puppet bandits and other troops in Chahar, they are determined to settle them militarily, seeking to realize this in the shortest possible time. Jia Deyao's previous trip to Zhang was in a private capacity, to meet with Feng to make some statements. After returning to Ping, he visited He Yingqin and Huang Fu last night to report on the course of this trip. Wu Yong, the director of the Chahar Civil Affairs Office, also arrived in Ping yesterday. This morning, the 10th, he visited Song Zheyuan. According to those close to Feng Yuxiang, Feng has always hoped that the anti-Japanese military affairs will be consistent with the central government, and that all Chahar provincial affairs will still be presided over by the lower government, with Feng personally willing to assist in everything. There has been much speculation about Feng in recent days. It has been rumored that Feng will finally go abroad, but this is an overstatement. (10th)

Suzhou

Two Shipping Vessels Robbed Midway

The two shipping vessels, Xu Genhu and Lu Achun, operating between Suzhou and Guangfu, were fully loaded with loquats. On the morning of the 12th, around 2:00 AM, they departed from Dongshan to Suzhou. While traveling about ten miles from Mu’du, near the Dongkuatang Bridge in Hengtang Township, they were suddenly encountered by a bandit boat carrying seven or eight bandits. The bandits blocked the road and robbed them. Two bandits, each holding a handgun, opened fire first. One bandit shot Lu Axiao, a crew member on Xu Genhu’s boat, in the right leg. They then robbed for about twenty minutes before leaving. The two boats were robbed of about twenty or thirty yuan in silver dollars. Fortunately, the remaining loquats and other goods were not lost. After the incident, the two boats opened to Suzhou and reported to the police station for investigation.

Silk Factory Resumes Operations, Labor Disputes

The Yanchangheng Silk Factory, located outside Fengmen, near Mudu Bridge, had previously ceased operations due to the decline in the silk market. The silk market has recently shown signs of improvement this year, so it continued operations.

However, the factory had over seven hundred male and female workers. Since the factory stopped operating, they had been unemployed for a long time. This time, when operations continued, they all hoped to return to work at the factory. However, the factory had already hired new workers, so they were greatly disappointed. They elected representatives to petition the Mudu Bridge Township Office, which in turn requested the county government for relief. Magistrate Zou especially ordered the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday (12th) and sent a letter to the County Party Headquarters to mediate and avoid disputes.

Defrauding Diamond Rings, Fleeing to Suzhou, Arrested

Chen Zong, twenty-eight years old, from Wuxi, recently defrauded Yunying, a prostitute at the China Hotel on Beijing Road in Shanghai, of two diamond rings. After pawning them in Shanghai, he fled to Suzhou and resided at the home of Jin Yuehua, a prostitute at No. 8 Minqing Lane outside the gate. After receiving a report, Captain Xu of the Anti-Banditry Department's Detective Team in this area dispatched detectives yesterday (12th) at 7:00 AM and successfully apprehended Chen Zong. They immediately took the team and presented him to the Anti-Banditry Department to await extradition to Shanghai for interrogation.

Wuxi

Petition to Strictly Limit Autumn Seed Quantity

The spring silkworm crop in the Wuxi area this year was excellent and of high quality. The price was also higher than in previous years. Silkworm farmers are pre-ordering autumn seeds and raising autumn silkworms in large numbers in the hopes of making a harvest in the sunset years. However, according to the statistics of the Silkworm Industry Control Office, the entire province of Jiangsu had more than 1.4 million sheets of spring seeds this year. If the harvest is good, there will be less elimination. According to the forecast, it will exceed the amount by 20%. The actual production will be at least 1.6 million sheets. According to the decision of the Silkworm Industry Control Committee to divide spring and autumn breeding as 30% and 70%, respectively, then this year's autumn seeds will total 956,000 sheets, which can be used for raising autumn silkworms in the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. However, various seed production farms, due to the strong sales of autumn seeds, have broken the 30-70 limit, and some have even produced all autumn seeds. Not only will spring seeds be lacking next year, but the limited mulberry leaves this year will inevitably cause great panic. Yesterday, Gu, the president of the Farmers Bank, together with the Provincial Public Education Institute, the County Party Headquarters, the Chamber of Commerce, the Agricultural Extension Institute, and the silk and cocoon guilds petitioned the Construction Department to strictly order all seed production farms to limit the amount of autumn seeds to no more than 60% to avoid the great danger of too many silkworms and too few leaves and a lack of spring seeds next year.

Shipping Industry Requests Exemption from Defense Donations

The various shipping companies in Wuxi received a letter from the County Defense Association informing them that starting in July of this year, they would begin collecting shipping donations, collecting five li with the ticket price. They convened a meeting yesterday to discuss the matter. They all believed that the shipping industry is currently in a slump. Routes such as Jiangyin have mostly been suspended. Even the few routes that are barely maintained are also reducing prices to attract customers. This is due to the collapse of the rural economy and the declining number of passengers. Many have stopped operating. If defense donations are collected again, it will inevitably affect passengers and make it even more impossible to maintain operations. They should follow the resolution of the previous County Chamber of Commerce meeting. The commercial sector has difficulty bearing the burden and requests that all collections be stopped. They have sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce requesting that it forward the letter to the county government to exempt the aforementioned defense donations.

Changshu

No One Responsible for Rural Teachers' School

This spring, the principal of Xitangqiao Rural Normal School, Qian Qin, became addicted to opium, and after being accused by local people, Qian resigned. The Education Bureau then recommended Shen Chenglie, the former director of the Changshu Education Bureau, to succeed him. However, after the appointment order was issued by the Education Department, Shen was unwilling to take office, and the appointment order was returned. As a result, for three or four months, no one was in charge of the Normal School. The two-year students are about to graduate, and the certificates will not have the signature of the person in charge of the school, which will definitely affect them in the future. They once went to the Education Bureau to petition, and then Ge, the director of the Education Bureau, personally went to Shanghai to urge Shen, the new principal, to cancel his resignation and take office immediately. Shen initially stated that he would take office after the summer vacation, and the school affairs would be temporarily handed over to the academic dean and the teaching staff. Unexpectedly, after a group discussion on the 10th, the teaching staff felt that the responsibility was too heavy and seemed inappropriate, so they decided to submit a collective resignation to the Education Bureau. As for the students, seeing that the teaching staff had expressed such an attitude, they were even more affected by the graduation, and the three-year students, although they had not yet finished this term, also opposed the Education Department's order to extend the three-year system by one year. Starting on the 12th of this month, they all went on strike, marched to the city in formation, and petitioned the county government.

Local News

Shanghai Municipality Levies Provisional Land Value Tax

Organization of Appraisal Committee

Submitted to the Executive Yuan for Approval

The Shanghai Municipality's Provisional Land Value Tax Regulations and the Appraisal Committee's Organizational Rules were previously submitted by the Executive Yuan to the Ministries of Interior and Finance for review. They have been revised, reported, and approved at the last 107th Executive Yuan meeting. They have also been consulted with the Legislative Yuan. A reporter from the Capital Zhengqi News Agency obtained the tax regulations and the appraisal committee rules yesterday and recorded them as follows:

Land Value Tax Regulations

Article 1: All land within the municipal commercial area shall, before the promulgation of the Land Law, be subject to a provisional land value tax levied in accordance with these regulations. The boundaries of the municipal commercial area shall be separately demarcated and announced.

Article 2: The following categories of land shall be exempt from the provisional land value tax: (1) Land owned by the municipality; (2) Land used for public charitable purposes without generating income, as approved by the municipal government for tax exemption.

Article 3: The provisional land value tax shall be paid by the owner of the land. In the case of land held under perpetual lease, the tax shall be paid by the holder of the perpetual lease. However, in cases involving mortgages, pledges, or fixed-term leases, the mortgagor, pledgee, or lessee may be required to pay the tax on behalf of the owner when necessary.

Article 4: The provisional land value tax rate shall be six per mille (0.6%) per annum, based on the assessed land value.

Article 5: The provisional land value tax shall be collected in two installments each year. The first installment shall be collected from January 1st to the end of February, and the second installment from July 1st to the end of August, both by the Bureau of Finance.

Article 6: To assess land values, the Land Bureau shall first survey the terrain and prevailing market prices, and consider the land values reported by the owners. The bureau shall then divide the land into valuation zones, and submit these to the Provisional Land Value Tax Land Valuation Committee for review. The valuation will be jointly announced by the Bureau of Finance and the Land Bureau. If an owner disagrees with the announced land value, they may submit a reasoned objection to the Land Bureau within the prescribed period, requesting arbitration by a public arbitrator. The regulations governing the Valuation Committee shall be separately stipulated.

Article 7: The collection of the provisional land value tax shall not be suspended due to an application for land value arbitration. However, the land value shall be adjusted according to the decision of the land value arbitrators once it is made.

Article 8: Failure to pay the provisional land value tax by the due date shall be deemed as tax arrears. A notice shall be served to demand payment, and a surcharge of 5% per annum on the amount owed shall be levied from the day following the expiration of the collection period. If the tax remains unpaid for more than three years, the collecting agency may, with the approval of the municipal government, auction the land and its fixtures to offset the tax arrears. Any remaining proceeds shall be returned to the original taxpayer.

Article 9: The original land tax and surcharges on land for which the provisional land value tax has been collected shall be abolished.

Article 10: Land within the area where the provisional land value tax is collected shall be subject to the land value tax simultaneously, regardless of whether it has been surveyed and registered. However, land that has not been surveyed and registered shall be subject to the temporary collection of land tax, and a receipt shall be issued. Upon completion of the survey and registration, the tax arrears shall be paid, and the owner may apply to the Land Bureau to have the receipt verified and used as a credit.

Article 11: For land certificates in areas where the provisional land value tax has been collected, the transfer tax payable when transferring land deeds shall be 2% of the market value. However, the methods for collecting the land appreciation tax and inheritance tax, which will be levied in the future when dealing with land transfers, shall be separately stipulated in accordance with the standards for dividing national and local land revenue.

Article 12: If any other levies or taxes in the area where the provisional land value tax is collected require changes to their rates or methods when the land tax is implemented, these shall be executed after the Land Law has been formally implemented.

Article 13: The assessed land value for the provisional land value tax shall be revised every three years.

Article 14: If changes to the area where the provisional land value tax is collected are deemed necessary, the municipal government shall redraw the boundaries and announce them.

Article 15: If increases or decreases in the provisional land value tax rate are deemed necessary, the municipal government shall revise the rate and submit it to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation.

Article 16: Detailed rules for the implementation of the regulations for collecting the provisional land value tax shall be stipulated separately.

Article 17: If there are any omissions in these regulations, the municipal government may revise them at any time and submit them to the Executive Yuan for approval and implementation.

Article 18: These regulations shall be promulgated and implemented after being submitted by the municipal government to the Executive Yuan for approval.

Valuation Committee Organization

Article 1: This committee is organized in accordance with the provisions of Article 6 of the Regulations for Collecting Provisional Land Value Tax in this city.

Article 2: The committee shall consist of five members, appointed by the mayor from among officials of the municipal government and the bureaus of finance, public works, social affairs, and land, who are familiar with land administration. The resumes of the members shall be submitted to the Ministry of Interior for record-keeping.

Article 3: The chairman of this committee shall be elected by the members.

Article 4: This committee may, as required by its work, appoint a number of clerks, drawn from the staff of various bureaus.

Article 5: This committee shall be temporarily located within the Land Bureau for convenience.

Article 6: The land price sections of each district, as provisionally estimated by the Land Bureau, shall be submitted to this committee along with maps for assessment. After assessment, they shall be submitted to the Bureau of Finance and the Land Bureau for approval by the municipal government before being jointly announced.

Article 7: Upon receiving the maps and tables of land price sections from the Land Bureau, this committee shall immediately convene a meeting of all members to review and assess them. The original staff of the Land Bureau shall attend the meeting to provide explanations. When necessary, staff shall be dispatched to conduct on-site investigations before reassessing.

Article 8: A quorum for meetings of this committee shall be more than half of the members. The assessment of land prices shall require the consent of a majority of the members present.

Article 9: If a member is unable to attend a meeting, they shall delegate a representative in writing.

Article 10: Meetings of this committee shall be convened by the chairman.

Article 11: These rules may be revised at any time if there are any omissions.

Article 12: These rules shall be implemented after being submitted by the municipal government to the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Finance for record-keeping.

Xiong Xiling

Yesterday's Reception for the Press

Report on the Huabei War Zone Relief Efforts

And Discussions with Various Sectors on Future Relief Measures

Xiong Xiling, President of the China General Association of the World Red Swastika Society and Vice Chairman of the Northeast Refugee Relief Association, hosted a reception for reporters from various newspapers at the Xinghua Restaurant on Fuzhou Road yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. He reported on the situation of the Huabei War Zone relief efforts and subsequent measures. More than 40 reporters from various newspapers attended and were personally received by Mr. Xiong. The details of the report are recorded below:

Relief Efforts During the Incident in Yuguan and Rehe

The Association formed 14 relief teams which were immediately dispatched to Chaoyang, Lingyuan, Kailu, Qinhuangdao and other places to provide relief to wounded soldiers and refugees. As Chengde fell and the war expanded, the original relief teams were insufficient to meet the needs. The Association convened a major relief conference of the All-China Red Swastika Society, deciding to expand the relief efforts, and added more than ten special relief teams, for a total of 27 teams before and after. I, along with Mr. Xu Lanzhou, personally led the teams to the Xifengkou, Lengkou, Luanxian, and Great Wall areas to intensify our work, providing both medical care for wounded soldiers and relief for refugees. In addition to running temporary hospitals in the rear to treat wounded soldiers, we also established more than ten refugee shelters in Beijing, Tianjin and Chahar, taking in refugees. Over three months, we spent more than 400,000 yuan. This money was jointly contributed by the Association's headquarters and various branches.

Post-Disaster Measures After my departure

the situation in Beijing and Tianjin became increasingly tense, and hundreds of thousands of refugees from various places fled to the Beijing and Tianjin areas. The Association added more than ten temporary shelters, accommodating more than 50,000 refugees. These refugees had mostly lost all their property and their homes were in ruins. Without thorough post-disaster measures for their current maintenance and future resettlement, they would have nothing to live on even after returning to their hometowns. Furthermore, during the height of the war, there were many casualties among the soldiers, the survivors were mostly disabled, and the families of the deceased were still awaiting support. Therefore, establishing rehabilitation centers for the disabled and providing compensation to the families of the fallen are also urgent matters. Since this war was not a formal declaration of war, international wartime laws were ineffective. Tens of thousands of corpses were scattered along the several thousand miles of the war zone along the Great Wall, all within the line of fire, and have not been adequately buried. Geographically, the Chahe River at Gubeikou, the Luanhe River at Xifengkou, the Ji Canal at Xinglong County, and the Shihe River at Shimenzhai all originate outside the Great Wall in Rehe Province. The rainy season in the north is at the end of May. If we do not take advantage of this ceasefire period to bury the dead, (even those who have already been buried, except for the soldiers of General Song's unit who died at Xifengkou, for whom the Association has built a public cemetery that is relatively well-maintained), the rest were hastily buried due to the intensity of the war and the urgency of time. Therefore, it is necessary to dig deeper and rebury them, both out of respect for humanity and for hygiene.

Jointly Launch Relief Efforts If heavy rains come

the corpses are swept into the river, the drinking water for the Chinese and foreign populations of Beijing and Tianjin will be at risk of contamination and disease. However, to seriously undertake this task in a war zone spanning thousands of miles, it will require more than a thousand laborers. Therefore, epidemic prevention work in the war zone must also be carried out immediately. The Association has already done its best to provide medical care on the front and rear lines, and the relief teams dispatched earlier are still working in various places to provide refugee shelter and treatment, not daring to slacken. However, the various issues mentioned above are extremely important and cannot be accomplished by the efforts of one association alone. Therefore, I have made a special trip to Shanghai to discuss with philanthropists in Shanghai future cooperative relief measures. Fortunately, I have received their approval and willingness to cooperate. It is expected that a Huabei War Zone Post-Disaster Relief Committee will be established to handle these matters. The relief tasks are numerous and complex, and require our joint efforts. Gentlemen of the press are all leaders of society, and have always been enthusiastic in supporting social welfare and various relief efforts. I hope that you will awaken people from all walks of life to jointly launch relief efforts, and I hope that you will provide guidance at any time so that we can complete the post-disaster work in the Huabei war zone. The suffering people of the time kowtow in request.

Results of Discussions With Reporters In response to questions about the results

of this trip to Shanghai, Mr. Xiong said that during the September 18th Incident, Zhang Xueliang lost the territory of the three northeastern provinces, an area of more than 400,000 square miles, due to his policy of non-resistance. The news spread far and wide, shocking the world. Whenever people from various countries inquired about it, I could only shake my head and sigh, unable to say anything. During the January 28th Incident, the 19th Route Army fought bravely against the Japanese, holding out for a month. Although a ceasefire agreement was signed due to various reasons, international prestige increased as a result, and I was very pleased. During the Yuguan and Rehe Incidents, our troops continued to resist, and General Song Zheyuan's division was the most valiant, with only over two thousand survivors. In total, more than 60,000 people were injured and more than 10,000 were disabled as a result of these battles. The people in the rear donated more than 60 million worth of rice, wheat, and firewood. It is appropriate to find solutions for these wounded soldiers and refugees so that the survivors will not be displaced. Therefore, after my arrival in Shanghai, I consulted with the Renji Hall and various parties, and found some leads. Philanthropists have generously stepped forward to help. Your publicity through speech is also no small contribution. Therefore, I have only prepared wine today to express my gratitude. I hope that the general public will unite sincerely and work together with one heart. The example of Goujian's defeat of Wu should serve as a warning. I am willing to work together with you to this end.

Dai Ji Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Office Work at Longhua Headquarters

Denies Representing Central Government in Fujian

The Second German Aircraft Arrived in Shanghai This Morning

Flying to Beijing Yesterday from Lanzhou

According to the Central News Agency, two new aircraft of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation arrived in China via Europe and Russia at the end of last month. One aircraft completed the test flight of the Eurasia route a few days ago and arrived in Shanghai. The other aircraft returned to Dihua to deliver the Xinjiang Envoy and arrived on the 10th and then returned east to Shanghai to complete the 10,000-kilometer Eurasia route. The aircraft took off from Lanzhou yesterday morning and arrived in Beijing at 7 pm, staying overnight and planning to come to Shanghai this morning, estimated to arrive around 10 am. According to the manager of the company, Li Jingcong, the German and Russian sides have reached an agreement on Eurasia joint transportation. If the Xinjiang rebellion can be quelled, it can fly to Tacheng in early July and connect with the Russian and German routes. Regarding the Northwest route, tomorrow (i.e. today) is the opening date, so it is decided to use the M-34 aircraft newly flown from Berlin, Germany, because its capacity is larger and it can carry more passengers and mail. However, after the aircraft has flown a long distance of 10,000 kilometers, it must be inspected to avoid mechanical failures. The inspection work is currently underway and will be completed tomorrow (i.e. today), so the sailing date has been postponed by one day and will depart on the morning after tomorrow (i.e. tomorrow morning).
