Novel

Four Company Commanders of Northeast China

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Is There a Reason for Jesting? The Son-in-Law Secretly Introduces Her

Why Did This Guest Come So Suddenly? The Western Teacher Leisurely Plots

Huang Manying's stay at the Yang's house for this one night gave the Jiang mother and daughter quite the jolt. Mrs. Jiang naturally stood on the side of supporting the matter of the woman. Even Guizhi herself was thinking that soldiers were not necessarily as bad as they thought of them to be. Look at Company Commander Tian, who Miss Huang was marrying, wasn't he also someone who had emerged from being a student? Although Company Commander Tang wasn't as lively and young as Company Commander Tian, he was honest and had a good number of desirable traits. Reflecting on the situation of Gan Jizhi through the lens of Zhao, that man was refined, and his appearance was quite handsome, but if you listened to what he was saying, the words did not line up as they should, wanting nothing more than to become an official and strike it rich, and would abandon all else, so, taking this into consideration, Zhao was actually the better of the two. Having this shift in perspective, when Miss Huang had asked Guizhi about it, the young woman found herself at a loss and unable to reply. After having eaten dinner, Mrs. Jiang quietly rented two Sanxin cotton quilts from the street to bring back, laying them on the other side of the kang bed, carefully preparing these two to be laid out to sleep on, yet putting the woman's own bedding on the opposite side, leaving a very large gap between them. Mrs. Jiang smiled at Manying and said, "We wouldn't dare to say that the rented quilts are clean. We'll have my daughter and I sleep here. Our own bedding was washed for the New Year, so you can rest assured as you sleep on it." As she spoke, she pointed with her hand in the direction of the kang bed. Manying let out a sound, "Ah-yo! Your treatment of me like this makes me so uneasy. Please arrange the bedding together. That way, I can also lie down with your eldest daughter and have a chat." Mrs. Jiang said with a smile, "We won't! You're a person who's gotten used to sleeping in an iron bed in the city, and now you're forced to sleep on an earthen kang bed after coming to our place. That's already putting you in a situation of discomfort, so how could we make it any worse?" Seeing that she was still being so courteous, the visitor took the initiative to walk forward and join the bedding together, clapping at the cotton quilts with her hand a few times, and said with a smile, "This is good! Let's sleep together along the way." As she spoke, she reached out to pull Guizhi's sleeve. Guizhi said with a smile, "You must be awfully uncomfortable at our place here, and now we want to squeeze you!" Manying said with a smile, "For you mother and daughter to say something like this, it's as if I'm the eldest miss. Eldest daughter, why don't you lie down, and that way, we can chat about whatever we want." The Jiang mother and daughter also felt that she had a very easy-going personality and could not refuse what she meant to do. So, Guizhi and Manying lay side by side along the kang bed, and Mrs. Jiang slept on the outside of Guizhi. Because Guizhi thought of Manying as a visitor coming from the city, she was afraid that she would be unhappy to sleep in the dark, so they did not extinguish the lamp. As the two of them struggled to keep their eyes open while lying on one end of the bed, there was no way to avoid speaking. (98)

From Gold to Love

— Ding Ming

While the hardness of gold may not match silver, it surpasses that of tin, ultimately making it the most precious of all metals. From this universally welcomed substance,

I perceive the entirety of love!

Gold's primary source is native gold, followed by gold-bearing pyrite, while telluride gold occurrences are quite limited. Similarly, in human relationships, love—natural love—is paramount, followed by love with some underlying motive, while love born from opposition and discord is exceedingly rare.

Gold's yellow, finely divided forms can transform into purple, red, dark brown, or black. It exhibits a yellow streak and is highly ductile and malleable. Thus, its uses extend beyond coinage, gold leaf production, fine wire drawing, and ornamentation to include the production of photographic chemicals and pigments for the glass and ceramics industries. This mirrors the intangible hues of love, beginning subtly with hints of pale blue, pale yellow, pale red, gradually evolving into rose, or pure white. Its capacity for diverse hues, coupled with its ductility and malleability, enables the other party's temperament, actions, learning, and instincts to be vividly and thoroughly colored. Eventually, this progresses to the white-hot phase of marriage.

Globally, gold's primary sources are the United States and Australia. In China, the now-lost Rehe province leads, with locations such as Sanchakou, Luanping, Badaohe, and Chaoyang. Liaoning follows, with Hailong Xiangluyingzi and others; Jilin, with Yanji Boge Yazijie and others; and Heilongjiang, with Jilalin Alaya Mohe, Kumar, and Wutonghe. Placer gold is also found along the banks of the Heilongjiang River and its tributaries. In Jilin, it's distributed across the Songhua River, Mudanjiang River, Ussuri River, and Suifen River basins. In Liaoning, it's found in the Liao River, Dayang River, and Ai River basins. Current territories of Hebei, Shandong, Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Fujian, Sichuan, Xikang, Tibet, (?), Mongolia, Xinjiang, Guizhou, and Yunnan provinces are all gold-producing regions. People's golden love starts from a smile? A question and an answer? A needle and a thread? A dish and a meal? A walk and a run? A shy blush and a burst of anger? A lament and a sob? A hum and a coo? A listening and a reading? A reach and a touch? ·······?

Or starts with a flick of clothing? Straightening a hat and combing hair? Riding horses and fencing? Playing soccer and swimming? Under the lamps and moonlight? In flower clusters and willow shadows? In mountain, water, pavilion and tower? Grinding and polishing? In the entertainment ground? In times of trouble? ······

However, one day gold may be worthless, and one day no one will speak of love. Isn't that the case in the primordial era of the opening of the universe?

Correction ·· The "lifting" character in the previous "Epidemic Two Documents Picking Up Tour Towns" was mistakenly written as the "inviting" character, and the "Five" character of the Wuzhou Pharmacy was mistakenly written as the "Asia" character. This is hereby corrected.

Wandering in Art

The Bitter Wine of Love

— Zha Wei

Love is a path that young men and women inevitably embark upon. But upon reflection, the taste of love is not always sweet; often, many people find the suffering felt during passionate love more profound and more cruel than the pain of unrequited love. Ms. Ai Xia is a woman of the times and a glittering star. Her writing is also clear and insightful. Recently, we have often seen her writings on love in newspapers and periodicals, which are incisive and insightful and are indeed the experiences of someone who has been through it. She has also written a screenplay, in which she plays the main character, which has now been filmed by the Star Film Company. The film is titled "A Modern Woman". The narrative of the story strikes a heavy blow to the young people who are immersed in the dream of love. In "A Modern Woman", she points out that love is a pointless deception, a hypocrisy, and that love is built on money. Young people with ambition should strive for their own future and not wander on the wrong path of love. Because love is only a small part of life!

"A Modern Woman" has been released in major cinemas in this city. This is a bitter wine of love, and I think young men and women should all be willing to taste it.

Who is Doing Art for Art's Sake?

— Liu Si

I believe that every member of the art world, whether in a grand gathering or in a casual conversation with two or three friends, if someone asks him, "Why are you doing art?" he will answer with particular solemnity: "I am doing art for art's sake"!

At the same time, I firmly believe that, in the art world, those who truly do art for art's sake are no more than one or two percent, and perhaps even that one or two percent should be discounted! The remaining 98 or 99 percent are doing art for a living and for money!

Is Ms. Hu Die, a film star who is good at singing and dancing, doing art for art's sake or for a living and for money? I dare not assert. But looking at the two songs about international society that she has recently sung, which others dare not and cannot sing, we can see that although she has not left the realm of doing art for a living and for money, we should at least admit that she is half doing art for art's sake.

Her songs are:

㈠ Don't you see "Green wine green, red lights red, jazz like a tide, youth like a dream, slender waist, outstretched wrist, like the willow in the wind. Don't you see... Dear sir! The entire northeast territory is lost! The blood of soldiers is still spilled on Shanghai Wusong!"

㈡ The last sound: "Dear sir, thank you for your kindness, forgive my restless heart, my restless mind, this is my last sound; you face this green wine and red lights, and think of the grievances and sorrows of the ghosts in the northeast! Don't wait until the country is broken and hatred lasts forever, sir, tonight's red mansion dream is not yet awake, look at the world boiling! Prepare, charge into the enemy's battle, I can no longer sink into dancing with you! Goodbye, my sir, we must have war! Liberate us in war! Fight to stain the earth with fresh blood, for the nation to fight for the last light!"

Singing such tragic and encouraging words to encourage the people to resist the enemy and save the country has indeed broken the new record of songs. Miss Hu's thoughts and insights are indeed superior to others!

These songs were recorded by the Baidai Company. When the record was being made, the manager of their company specially invited some friends who loved art to come and visit. I was one of the invitees, so I discovered two characteristics of Hu Die's singing of these songs:

㈠ Hu Die's voice is originally clear and crisp and can be high and low, strong and soft; on this day, when she sang, I felt that it was even more desolate and full of flavor, probably because of "concentrating her mind".

㈡ These two songs both use Western music to play Chinese opera tunes! Don't you see that "Nan Bangzi" uses the "Jazz Waltz" beat, and the last sound is "Er Liu", which uses the Fox-trot dance music. When Hu Die sings, she can fit the music everywhere, and at the same time, she can maintain the essence of Peking opera, which is indeed particularly "rare and valuable".

Free Talk

Respectful Thanks for Development

— Zheng Boqi

Ever since the friendly friends from the East brought giant cannons from the Northeast, we Chinese have had two great inventions... One is "Long-term Resistance", which has long been world-renowned, and we won't talk about it. The other is "Development of the Northwest", which even most Chinese people have not yet understood. Because of my hometown relationship, I know a little more, so I can't help but publicize it to everyone.

You see, since September 18th, haven't we added two capital cities? Chang'an, which has been dead for thousands of years, has also become a secondary capital. Since then, the call for "Development of the Northwest" has been as loud as the sound of cannons from the Northeast.

Many important people go to the Northwest, industrial survey teams go to the Northwest, journalists go to the Northwest, and even the Shanghai playboys who have always regarded the Northwest as the African desert are clamoring to go to the Northwest. In ancient times, Confucius went west but did not enter Qin. The modern figures of the 20th century have made great progress after all.

Under such vigorous promotion, if the Northwest is still plagued by war and famine, then the Northwest is really content to lag behind. Sure enough, according to old hometown folks who have recently come from there, the situation in the Northwest is indeed different from before. Gold has almost disappeared from the market, and even the Qin bricks and Han tiles excavated from the countryside have greatly increased in price. The Chinese banknotes there have a very great "development" effect. Where has the gold that has been hidden in cellars for hundreds of years gone? It is now probably studying abroad in the basement of the New York Bank. As for the Qin bricks and Han tiles, although they cannot go east to Fusang to taste the flavor of the Imperial Museum for the time being, they can at least see the bright electric lights and the towering foreign buildings on the Shanghai Bund. This is of course something that they are happy about, as they have never seen the world.

Moreover, there are also extremely fragrant stories here.

It is said that a certain noble lady once took a plane from the duty station of her husband in a certain northwest province to Beijing, and the airline had to weigh her weight as usual. Perhaps this company is a "Citibank" brand, so even the noble lady could not express her anger and had to bow her head and let people weigh her. Unexpectedly, it was okay if she didn't weigh, but once she weighed, the petite and exquisite lady, who could dance on her palm, actually weighed one hundred and eighty pounds. Perhaps you will suspect that she has a little treasure in her belly, but her belly is not big, but her waist is a little thicker. What is strange is that after she returned to the south, the price of gold in Shanghai changed.

Therefore, many of my hometown folks are afraid of the slogan "Development of the Northwest". They feel that it is better not to develop, and once developed, both gold and rubble will have a share in going abroad, which is really something they dare not accept.

Regarding "Three-Story Building" and "Antiques" Reply to Mr. Da Wu

— Hu Qiuyuan

I just saw Mr. Da Wu's question about the translation of my humble work in Free Talk, and I was surprised and grateful. Although I am quite cautious when translating books, there are really many omissions. After that book by Iko 維持 was translated into Japanese, my friend Mr. Fang Tianbai and I translated it together. At that time, I also got a copy of the original text, but we only knew a few words of French, so in addition to adding people's names and book names, we only checked the original text in detail when we encountered places where the Japanese translation was too difficult to understand. For example, I carefully reviewed the "Egyptian beans" in the article on creation organization. After the book was translated, it could not be sold, and then several translations came out, and the original manuscript became useless. After writing the art theory, I submitted one of the articles as an appendix, but I did not go to look at it in detail. I admit that the translation of the "Three-Story Building" passage is wrong and is a mistake. The Japanese translation is completely consistent with Mr. Dai Wangshu's translation. The Japanese translation has large characters, "which unfolds in three stages." Japanese characters and Chinese characters are the same, I would not fail to recognize the three characters "three stages." But I overlooked it at the time and dropped the character "stage," so it became "three levels." "Three levels" is the Japanese meaning of "three-story building." So the mistake came from seeing "three stages" as "three levels." However, it is true that a miss of a hair's breadth results in an error of a thousand miles.

However, regarding the three characters "antiques," Mr. Da Wu need not be so picky. Although the original text is not at hand, Mr. Dai translates it as "long miscellaneous." The Japanese translation is "antiques," and I also use the two characters "antiques," which is correct. When Mr. Da Wu sees the two characters "antiques," he immediately thinks of the "antiques" of Shandong and Henan. In fact, the original meaning of "antiques" is "zero miscellaneous," and food that is cooked in a miscellaneous way is called "antique soup." The ancient objects are called "antiques," which is a later meaning, because the sound of the three characters "ancient bronze" is transferred. Mr. Da Wu thinks that "antiques" must be dug out of the earth, why bother?

There are roughly three sources of translation errors: first, pretending to know what you don't know; second, not checking the dictionary and interpreting the meaning of the words literally; third, misreading or dropping words. Like the last one, I don't think it should be attacked so severely.

Ode to the City God Temple

Lin Yizhi

Forty or fifty rickshaws drove westward in a long line from Xiaodongmen. The passengers were all high-nosed, blue-eyed Westerners, said to be some kind of tourists from foreign countries, going to visit the City God Temple. Foreigners are smarter after all. They know that the tall white stone houses along the Bund and the green lights and red buildings on Avenue Joffre are only the skin of Shanghai. To really understand the heart of Shanghai, you have to go to the City God Temple.

The City God Temple is filled with hazy incense smoke. In the hall with yellow walls and carved corners rebuilt with steel bones and cement, the City God Bodhisattva in Song Dynasty costumes sits majestically. However, those who bow down before him are modern ladies with Parisian perfume on their bodies, American leather shoes on their feet, and hairstyles permed in the 1933 style. They really understand the principle of Chinese learning as the foundation and Western learning for application. Like the generals who ride in Ford airplanes, they are still wholeheartedly treating the virtuous with courtesy, setting up a stage to recruit heroes from all over the world, and soliciting talents who can fly and walk on walls in order to jointly meet the national crisis. The City God Temple is the most popular entertainment place. Just as the upper-class Chinese in Shanghai have their Mingyuan, Liva, and Dada Village, the lower-class Chinese in Shanghai have their City God Temple. The small books that cost three or five copper coins a piece are full of paintings and words. They all invite chivalrous men and sword immortals who will draw their swords to help when they see injustice on the road. In a society where you can easily be slapped in the face by foreigners, these heroes are of course a great comfort. So, some young shop assistants are determined to go to Mount Emei to cultivate Taoism so that they can come back and take revenge on their masters and teachers, and they can also fight against the Japanese and save the country. Secondly, it costs six copper plates to see the big-headed people, the small-headed people, and the spider spirits. These things are excellent substitutes for people who cannot even afford two dimes to go to the cinema to see Hollywood legs. Like Hollywood legs, they can make people forget the painful reality and get the intoxication of enjoyment.

The City God Temple is also a popular Sincere and Wing On. Most of the people in Shanghai who can only look at the department stores outside the glass cabinets can satisfy their desires in the City God Temple. A glass ring that costs two dimes will also shine brightly. So, although they see diamonds worn on other people's bodies, they can also comfort themselves with glass light and do not have to feel any unfairness towards others.

The City God Temple also replaces the Royal Hotel and Sullivan. It is said that the taste of Changshu fermented rice balls, Nanxiang steamed buns, white sugar lotus root porridge, and gluten and bean curd leaves cannot be found anywhere in the world, but the City God Temple can satisfy you. The dark crowd is filled with dark stalls, and together with the seeds of flies and all kinds of bacteria, they swallow these delicacies into their hungry stomachs, cultivating powerful antitoxins and engaging in long-term resistance to germs. It is said that this is the unique ability of the Chinese nation to continue its race.

If you are interested, go up to Chunfeng Deyilou or Huxinting to drink tea, and you will better understand the greatness of the Chinese national character. Next to the stinking urine place, someone is tasting tea and talking or sitting alone in meditation. In the midst of a noisy crowd and hot sweat, someone is pulling the erhu to play music or blowing the xiao to tell their feelings. Some people face the streets and alleys where pedestrians are mixed, raising their delicate eyes and adjusting their voices, and some people take a few small newspapers and grab some spiced pumpkin seeds and licorice Huang Lian head and send them into their mouths.

Although in the downtown area, it is like being far away from the dust. If you understand the samadhi here, you can be a good citizen of a great Chinese country. But this spirit is said to have a source, which is a lake in the City God Temple. This lake has a Jiuqu Bridge with nine-curved railings. Under the bridge flows mud-like water, which is evaporated by sunlight and emits a dark light, releasing a burst of stench. The Japanese writer Ryunosuke Akutagawa once personally saw someone urinating in this lake. In fact, things that are even more evil than urine are thrown into this lake. But this is a famous scenic spot listed in the Chinese Grand View, (just as the Great Wall, although it is knocked on the finger as the new border of "Emerging Manchuria", is still a Chinese scenic spot under the determination to recover it,) so the turtles living in this lake still believe that they are in a famous scenic spot, swimming leisurely and contentedly. Sometimes, although they raise their heads to breathe on the surface of the water, perhaps they feel that it is too turbid, but after a while, they lower their heads again and enjoy it happily.

This great spirit of the turtle has indeed made a great contribution to the Chinese nation. Therefore, the City God Temple is ultimately a Shanghai public education hall.

No wonder it was burned down once a few years ago, and many gentlemen generously donated money and immediately rebuilt it. No wonder the Westerners who come to Shanghai to visit want to visit the City God Temple first!

Drought

— Yi Fei

Wang Lao Si stood on the pond road, staring absently at the pond that had dried up to the bottom, and his own rice fields waiting for rain. He had no choice but to sigh helplessly.

The early summer sun was already scorching hot on his back, causing him to sweat constantly. The high and clear sky showed no sign of rain.

"Yes, the weather has changed. The season has just entered summer, and the sky has been clear for so long!" Wang Lao Si said to himself, pacing back and forth on the pond road.

Indeed, this was something that had never happened in recent years. A drought broke out just when the rice was planted!

—Of course, his own rice fields were too close to the mountains and fields, and the wheat ripened too slowly, so the nearby ponds were dry when it was time to plant the rice. But if it continued to be sunny like this, what would be the use even if it had already been planted? Thinking about it, Wang Lao Si remembered what happened last year:

—Wasn't last year a year of "favorable weather" and "abundant harvests"? However, the cheap price of grain caused him, who had been struggling to survive in the soil all year round, to incur a large debt: He had originally hoped to "recover his capital" this year, but what would be the result this year? Just when he started planting rice, it had been sunny for so long, and a drought had broken out!

—Ah—this year that always makes it difficult for the poor! Is poverty, disease, and hunger really the only reward for us honest and law-abiding farmers? ······

He kept thinking, and sweat filled his whole body in the hot and dry air. He looked up at the sky, and the sky was still high and clear, without any sign of rain.

Carrot Whiskers

— Written by Julcs Kenard, Translated by Lin Qu

Tadpole

Carrot Whiskers was playing alone in the yard. He was standing in the middle of the yard so that the Lepeck family could watch him from the window. He was playing very well when his friend Remy came running over. Remy was a child of the same age as him. Although he was a cripple, he always wanted to run, so his bad left foot often fell behind the other one, never catching up. He was carrying a basket and said:

"Are you coming, Carrot Whiskers? Dad soaked the hemp in the river. Let's go help him and use the basket to catch tadpoles."

"You go ask my mom," Carrot Whiskers said.

Remy—Why should I ask?

Carrot Whiskers—Because if I ask, she won't let me.

Just then, the Lepeck family stuck their head out of the window and looked over.

"Mrs. Lepeck, can I take Carrot Whiskers to catch tadpoles?" Remy said.

The Lepeck family put their ears to the glass. Remy called out the words above again. The Lepeck family understood. We saw her moving her lips. The two children didn't hear anything and could only look at each other hesitantly. But the Lepeck family shook their heads at this time, clearly indicating that they would not allow it.

"She doesn't agree," Carrot Whiskers said. "She must have something for me to do right away." Remy—It's a pity, otherwise everyone could have had a good time playing. She doesn't agree, she doesn't agree.

Carrot Whiskers—Stay here. Let's play together here.

Remy—Ah! No, who would do that? I would rather go fishing for tadpoles. The weather is very mild. I can catch several baskets full. Carrot Whiskers—Wait a little while. Mom often refuses at first. Sometimes she changes her mind later.

Remy—I'll wait a little while, but not much more.

The two put their hands in their pockets and stood there together, staring intently at the ladder. After a while, Carrot Whiskers pushed Remy with his elbow and said:

"See, what did I tell you?"

Indeed, the door opened, and the Lepeck family was holding a basket prepared for Carrot Whiskers in their hand, and took a step down. But she hesitated and stopped.

"Hey, you're still here, Remy· I thought you were gone. I'll tell your dad later that you're playing wild outside, and he'll scold you."

Remy—Carrot Whiskers asked me to wait for him.

Lepeck family—Ah! Really, Carrot Whiskers?

Carrot Whiskers neither admitted nor denied it. He didn't know what to do. He understood the Lepeck family thoroughly, and he guessed her again. But Remy, that stupid thing, had completely ruined the good thing, and Carrot Whiskers didn't care about the ending of this matter. He trampled the grass on the ground with his feet, looking elsewhere.

"But I don't seem to have the habit of changing my mind," the Lepeck family said. (To be continued)

Silk Tea: Qimen Tea Shops Stop Making Zi Tea

Qimen black tea is divided into spring and summer first tea and zi tea. Each company has finished making spring village and is taking care of summer village. The output of zi tea is not as huge as that of the first tea, but it is also not in a small number. This year, spring tea in Qimen and Fu both suffered losses, and prices fell again. Mountain households lost tea and lost prices, hoping that the Shanghai market would improve. Zi tea production was abundant, making up for the previous shortage. Qimen Tea Industry Association received a telegram from the Shanghai Association, saying that foreign merchants were trying to depreciate tea prices and sales were narrow. Please stop making zi tea to avoid losses. Therefore, all tea companies that had finished making first tea and planned to make zi village ended there and did not add any more. Mountain households who are about to open gardens to pick and make zi tea all feel deeply that it is difficult to support their lives.

Conversation

Small-Mindedness

— Tianfang

Recently, I've been a bit paranoid, constantly thinking with unease, "It's coming," "This time it's really coming," and I can't be at peace. Although I haven't personally been persecuted in any way, from what I vaguely see around me, I feel that this sense of "it's coming" isn't unfounded. Really, in this abnormal China, it's not easy, it's not easy to make you think positively. In my imagination of the future, the pleasing aspects are far fewer than the frightening ones. I always feel like it's late in the evening, with twilight attacking from all sides, and a darker situation is about to unfold before my eyes, so I am terrified. It might be a bit "small-minded," but reality forces you not to have any hope. A few days ago, I went to Jiangwan to see an airshow as per a friend's invitation. The pilot's smooth and skillful flying really moved me. It is said that the Aviation Association has ordered eighteen fighter planes—I am also one of the two-yuan bosses, but I don't care—I can't manage these idle accounts, but whether or not one is a shareholder or boss, one always has the right to imagine. I thought, if I could fly these eighteen planes to Tokyo and Osaka to retaliate for some of the damage from the Shanghai battle and the grievances of the people of Northeast China, wouldn't that be a satisfying thing? But as soon as I thought that we are "ill-fated Chinese," I immediately stopped the thought, feeling that such an idea was a bit too presumptuous. The era has reached the 20th century, and airplanes should have originally been possessed by civilized countries as embellishments of a prosperous age. But using them to carry important people, or circling the city three times in the air, and spreading it to ordinary wealthy people to broaden their horizons, is also good, right? We also have the opportunity to appreciate them. But now the situation has changed again, and the "it's coming" that I was probably worried about is finally coming. Then, even if you are not very at ease, there is nothing you can do about it. In this turbulent situation, the planes will naturally be put to use. Although it is unknown which way the bombs will fall, it can be asserted that the tails will not point inward. Although hoping for this is "small-minded, judging the heart of a gentleman with one's own," it originally does no harm to the sun and moon. If, unfortunately, it turns out to be true, then it would be an unexpectedly terrible thing.

Literary Arts

Four Rhymes

— Bai Jiao

I entered Huaxu and traveled around China, hearing children's rhymes that go like this:

Drawing Promises, Drawing Promises

The world is astonished, Champagne is offered, Loquats have no feet, How can one eat their flesh without peeling the skin?

Children's Rhyme from a Farming Village

Sweet trees have worms, felled by themselves and collapsing, Golden beetles hurt my crops, Countless coming from the west, Who cares about me, Officials in Guangzhou are carefree,

Buying Chicken Rhyme

Buying chickens that don't fly, Thieves are coming with hope, Brothers are there, With thick arms and big fists, Urging eggs,

Good Year Rhyme

In a good year, people suffer from hunger, Or manage their graves, Go out and see farmers dying on the road, Saying the blue sky remains the same,

Restaurant Xishi

— Warrior

A Zhen brought the dinner again.

Because of the meal problem, everyone really felt troubled. They paid a high price but couldn't get good food. "Contract meals are not fit for humans!" They often complained about the contract meals.

Because everyone's opinions differed, Zhao Shangyuan and Quan Sheng gathered three or four people and formed a small group, eating at He Xing, a small contract meal place in Lane 33 behind. He Xing is not large. Besides the owner and his wife, there is also the owner's daughter, named A Zhen. There is also a hired hand. Because there are few people, A Zhen always personally delivers the contract meals to the small tables recently. A Zhen is nineteen years old this year. Although she may not necessarily be very delicate, she is slender enough, with a white face, bright and shiny eyes, red lips, and thin eyebrows, all of which show her youthful beauty. Especially her legs and arms are particularly plump and white. The snow-white, thin gauze stockings wrapped her legs tightly, as if they were about to burst. Inside, a faint pink flesh color was revealed, and it seemed as if a scent of meat wafted over with every movement. Several young men in these alleys then jointly gave her the title of "Restaurant Xishi." The young friends in several nearby small shops all wanted to flirt with her, and A Zhen was really unrestrained, never afraid of these young friends' entanglement.

Quan Sheng was also one of those drooling over A Zhen. Now that they had contract meals with He Xing, and it happened to be A Zhen delivering the meals herself, this was naturally a good opportunity for Quan Sheng. Although they had only been eating the contract meals for three to five days, the results of Quan Sheng's advances were not bad.

When eating, Zhao Shangyuan and a few older people were present. Quan Sheng couldn't be too presumptuous. He just secretly glanced at A Zhen with his eyes. A Zhen naturally leaned against the window, watching them eat. She knew that Quan Sheng was peeking at her, and her watery eyes then gave Quan Sheng a slight smile. Quan Sheng couldn't resist A Zhen's gesture, and his heart suddenly pounded, and he felt a whooshing sound in his ears.

Quan Sheng finished his meal quickly. Today, he couldn't endure it any longer. He quickly walked to the corner of the back alley. It happened that there were no electric lights installed here, and the place was very dark, with few people coming and going. In Quan Sheng's view, it was the perfect place to intercept someone. What happens next can only be told after asking Quan Sheng.

Isn't this the special benefit of eating contract meals?

Little Sanzi's Home

— Leji

In a certain district north of Shanghai, there is a very large (not a large scale) slum. The houses are made of piles of broken bricks and mud walls, and roofs of mixed grass and reeds. Looking at them from a distance, one would never think that they are places where breathing people live, but rather like tombs where people from another world rest. Eighty or ninety percent of the residents inside are friends who pull rickshaws or wheelbarrows. Our Little Sanzi is one of them. Now I will ask him to come out as a representative to show a glimpse of the living conditions here.

His house is a room of less than two zhang square, and his whole family of five eats, drinks, and sleeps in it. Besides a south-facing door that requires one to bend down to enter, there is also a hole in the north side that is less than a foot in diameter and not quite round. When the door is closed, it can still let in some light. The roof above has long lost its function, only blocking the sun's heat, while wind and rain can freely invade. When it rains, the whole house is always filled with water, and if you are not careful, you will be woken up from a good dream by the rain. Such a place would probably be considered unhygienic even for dogs to come and go, but if they don't live here, where else can they go? Moreover, they are struggling outside all day for a living and have no time to take care of cleaning the house. A table with wobbly legs, two broken bamboo chairs, a cracked jar stove, two uneven beds made of broken wooden planks, and miscellaneous things with no place to be placed. There are also several bowls and plates that have turned black, broken stands, washbasins, and pieces of wood, iron cans, and the like scattered everywhere. The whole house is in a state of chaos, with dirty colors and a moldy smell. You will probably vomit for three days after entering for a minute, but they seem to be used to it and never disgusted. The concept of hygiene is something they don't have.

During the day, the house is always quietly closed because their whole family always sets out early in the morning on a journey for a living and will not return until sunset. He himself pulls a rickshaw, his wife is a seamstress, a daughter helps her mother, and two sons spend all day outside picking up scraps with bamboo baskets on their backs. They are truly self-reliant and a family that cooperates by division of labor. Although each person's face inevitably bears the deep marks of struggling with life, sometimes you can also see his sons each holding a bowl of yellow rice, with a piece of bright red, sauce-like pork on top, eating with a very satisfied smile. This probably indicates that their business has been good these days, or that their sons have picked up something valuable. At this time, their happiness is probably beyond what even princes and grandsons can reach!

My Enlightenment

— Zhang Yiping

I remember seeing a "New World Fifty Years Later," where people's names were completely replaced by Signal and other designations. Although it's just imagination, a person's name is ultimately just a symbol. Zhang San and Li Si only make people think of a thin, tall person when Zhang San is mentioned, and a short, fat person when Li Si is mentioned. If someone like Chiang Kai-shek is only referred to as Chairman Chiang, and Zhang Xueliang is called Zhang the Non-Resister, it's because the latter titles are well-known and have almost become their reporters. I never thought that my deceased father's name for me, "Ping," would become fashionable this year. Every magazine, every supplement, has the discovery of the character "Ping," and the "News" supplement even has the same name signed as "Yiping." I don't dare to take credit for others' work, nor am I willing to change the character "Ping" that has accompanied me for twenty-five years. While I was in a dilemma, yesterday (the 9th), an advertisement for "Yiping Jian" was found in the "Shen Bao" again, causing my friends to rush to my little house to ask me what was going on. The newspaper advertised: "Received the letter and rushed over at night, searched everywhere in Hangzhou and Beijing without finding you, returning to Quzhou, I am restless, staying in Hangzhou, my vacation is about to end, if I delay any longer, both public and private matters will be harmed, could this be what you initially expected, fortunately, upon seeing this newspaper, return home immediately," etc. I was afraid that even worse discoveries would be made, so I painfully sacrificed and changed the "Ping" that had accompanied me for twenty-five years to "Pin." Friends, please recognize the trademark so that there is no mistake. (Thank you)

The Power of Hunger

— Daren

Hunger truly has an unbelievable and amazing power. Just one day without eating, and your stomach will start to rebel. No matter how strong your will is, it will make you dizzy, your vision blurry, and your limbs weak. You must find something to comfort that empty stomach. At this time, as long as it can comfort and suppress the rebellious stomach, any method or means can be chosen. No matter how strict the law, how thorough the police, or how much morality maintains people's hearts, they all lose their effectiveness in the face of hunger. Law, police, and morality, I feel, are only tools for binding the mediocre people who are well-fed and warmly clothed, and can never bind the hungry masses who devour everything like tigers and wolves. "A gentleman in poverty" is just black words on white paper. In fact, there is no such thing. As long as hunger descends upon him, all those so-called moral, conscientious, and law-abiding people will act against their principles. "When the granaries are full, people know etiquette," and "when people are well-fed and clothed, they know honor and shame." These two sentences are eternal truths. I often hear the cries of "selling children and daughters" and the tragic events of "exchanging children to eat," which are already the most cruel things in the world. But who knew that during the famine in Gansu and Shaanxi two years ago, there were actually people who "cut off their beloved son's thin legs to use as lunch and cut open their beloved wife's nipples to temporarily use as dinner!" Even their beloved wives and children were being cut and opened, and there was no need to mention other laws that were merely empty words and the morality of human hearts that spoke empty words. Hunger truly has an unbelievable and amazing power! She roars like a sea wave, wanting to submerge everything! It roars like a lion, wanting to devour everything! Aren't the masses of China now trapped in a tragic state of hunger and cold?

My Daughter-in-Law is Good!

I Want My Son!

Mr. Editor,

Your column is like the red and green traffic lights on the road. Since its birth, I don't know how many problems it has solved. I have a matter concerning my children and grandchildren that I would like to ask you about. I think you will definitely not refuse. The facts are like this: I am an old accountant in a silk and cloth shop. I have two sons. The younger one is still in middle school, and the older one is twenty-two years old this year. In 1929, I arranged a marriage for him. At that time, their feelings did not seem incompatible. Soon after, my son joined the military in early 1930 due to difficult family circumstances and is now serving in the political department of a certain army. He usually sends two letters home every month, and at least one. This year, because his grandmother was seriously ill, I wanted him to come home once, but I was greatly disappointed. His reply said, "Unless I declare my divorce from the woman you arranged, don't think about me coming home, and from now on, I will stop sending letters to show my determination," etc. Indeed, it has been three or four months since then, and there has been no letter. In my opinion, he must be bewitched by some free love. Mr. Editor, this matter makes me angry and not angry. His wife is hardworking at home, extremely patient, has an intelligent mind, and manages all the affairs of the household. Furthermore, she has none of the extravagant habits of modern women. In this case, what should I do? If I don't let her divorce him, my hateful son will definitely not realize his mistake. If I let her divorce him, it would not only be morally wrong, but it would also not be legally permitted. In this dilemma, how can I make my hateful son realize his mistake? Is it possible to let her divorce him? I think you have great knowledge and will definitely solve it for me. Finished, wishing you peace in editing. Wu Shenwu sincerely

X X X

Editor's Note: In our opinion, this matter is not difficult for Mr. Wu. Whether your son and daughter-in-law divorce or not is purely their own business. You not only have no right to interfere, but even if you want to, you can't control it. If they want to divorce, even if your daughter-in-law is good, you cannot force them to stay together. If they don't want to, you should send a letter to your son, explaining that the matter of divorce must be discussed in person upon his return. As a father, you cannot do it for him. At the same time, give your son's letter to your daughter-in-law so that she knows her husband's attitude. After your son receives the letter, whether he returns or not is up to him. As for your daughter-in-law, the three attitudes she takes below are all legal. 1) She can file a lawsuit with the court based on the letter, remarry, and reserve the right to claim damages. 2) She can sue in court. You can file a lawsuit with the competent court where the marriage is registered. After acceptance, the court can send a document to the court where your son is employed to assist. However, this procedure often has difficulties in being shelved. Therefore, if she has the power, she can go to the court or military court to which your son currently belongs to file a lawsuit, which is more powerful. 3) She pretends not to notice and remains in your residence as if nothing happened. In this case, her marital relationship with your son continues to exist. At any time when your son returns, she can file a lawsuit for abandonment or bigamy. The second method above is of course the toughest, and I hope she doesn't take it. The third method seems gentle on the surface, but it is absolutely contrary to your desire to "want your son to return." Therefore, you might as well express this desire when you hand your son's original letter to your daughter-in-law. If she agrees, then the divorce is set, and your son will be willing to return. The remaining issue of compensation will be borne by your son. However, the matter of divorce is best resolved through negotiation. Going to court is unavoidable. So you need to tell your son to come back and discuss it in person. When you write to your son, you must clearly and repeatedly explain this.

We have always advocated that for divorce, it is better to separate frankly than to sleep in the same bed with different dreams. However, we advocate that those who are arbitrarily abandoned should bear considerable responsibility.

Correction: Due to the author's carelessness, the page numbers of the original manuscript were not clearly indicated, resulting in a disordered sequence. Therefore, upon hearing that a page was missing from Section 8, a passage was immediately added temporarily. Who knew that this passage would later be published again in Section 10. The following corrections are now made: Please discard "I don't know when... it would be nice to marry him" from line 26 of Section 8. "Feeling emotional... it would be nice to marry him" from after line 12 of Section 10 "Not appealing this way" should be inserted into the blank space of Section 8. As for the number "feeling emotional" at the end of line 25 of Section 8, please also remove it and connect it to form the phrase "But because of laziness..." "Not appealing this way" in line 12 of Section 10 is followed by "This demon..." in line 23 of the same section. I am very ashamed. In addition to the corrections, I would like to apologize to the readers and editors.

Fiction

The Life of the Five Beauties (3) (11) (1) (Continued)

— Linghe

Twenty-Eight, Revenge (2)

Suddenly, Zhang Wenbin walked out from inside, elegant and refined, bowing respectfully to the two tycoons separately. Then, he calmly handed a roll of documents to Su Gengyun and opened a collotype printing for them to look at a few pages. He said:

"The original manuscript of the documents will of course be returned, but a copy like this should be kept as a souvenir because it is the most precious treasure in Chinese diplomacy and also ironclad proof of your patriotic enthusiasm."

Once crisis, from then on peace returned.

Twenty-Nine, After the Success of the Revolution

From then on, many years passed, until the Fifth Madam was already twenty-seven years old. Counting from the Chinese Revolution, it has already been five years. Now that the revolution has taken place, the government must make big changes. Of course, Minister Su also said that he was unhappy to interact with the revolutionaries, so this is one of the most significant political achievements after the revolution. To put it more clearly, it is as Wu Gui said: "A country without an emperor is already unheard of, but who knew that now even the president is not needed? 'Chairman,' even the tone is not loud enough. Moreover, instead of establishing a capital in Beijing, which has the imperial palace, they insist on moving from Wuhan to Nanjing, Nanjing to Luoyang, and Luoyang back again. It's simply like children playing around. In short, these years have become more and more unreasonable, even changing Beijing to Beiping. And the four northeastern provinces have been leased to Japan."

Of course, people like Wu Gui can't understand anything, they don't understand the mysteries of the government. But even though such a person is thinking wildly, he has not been arrested and imprisoned, probably because civil rights have long been guaranteed.

However, there is one thing that makes Wu Gui very happy, and that is that young master Zhang has actually been promoted from first secretary to director of the intelligence department in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. So the Fifth Madam is filled with joy, Wu Gui follows her joy, and there is also a He Xiang who is secretly happy. Precisely because Zhang Wenbin cannot often leave Nanjing, the Fifth Madam has recently bought a foreign house in Tangshan, which is considered a summer resort.

As for Grandpa Su Gengyun, he is still as busy as before. Although he refuses to officially take the stage again as a minister, he cannot help but come out to help when national disasters occur. He always has to give ideas on important diplomatic cases.

However, he has become much older in these years. The Fifth Madam also rarely has the interest to come often, but in accordance with the "agreement," she is still paid 100,000 yuan per month by the Bank of Taiwan.

Therefore, if we put ourselves in his shoes, this old gentleman with high morals is indeed too pitiful.

Once, Minister Su happily came to Shanghai from Beijing. In addition to state affairs, he naturally wanted to be close to the Fifth Madam. This day, he bought two new pieces of clothing for her and happily accompanied the Fifth Madam for a few days. Although the summer days were long, they passed quickly and happily. Last night, he played a game of Jai Alai for the whole night and was inevitably very tired. Both of them slept until the afternoon. Then he suggested going to see Mei Lanfang's "Wild Mountain Tears," which he had performed after getting his doctorate from the United States. Who knew that at 4:00 PM, the Fifth Madam was sitting at her dressing table when she suddenly received a telegram from Zhang Wenbin in Nanjing, telling her to take the night train immediately. So she told the maid to pack her suitcase and told the old man:

"I have to go to Nanjing now. You stay at home for a few days. We'll go see the play another day."

"But," he said angrily, "I traveled all the way from Beijing, can't you spend a few days playing with me?"

"That won't work. People have things to do. Who cares about watching?"

Sadly, upon hearing these words, he had no choice but to remain silent.

Tuesday (5)

Movie Special

"Technocracy" in Hollywood Thoughts (Part 2)

— Zhuxian

When it comes to these Hollywood stars, regarding their attitude towards Technocracy, we must first remember their background. The big stars of Hollywood are all lucky ones. Their earnings can be as high as one or two million dollars per week. Therefore, they are not willing to give up their current superior position and work like everyone else, earning only $20,000 a year. But in Hollywood, there are still many workers who work hard all year round, and their income is less than a big star's daily earnings. Under this great disparity and unequal situation, what are their feelings? Let's examine it from various aspects.

One day at Pickfair, the residence of Fairbanks and Pickford, many stars gathered. After tea and dinner, little Fairbanks brought up the question of "supporting or opposing" Technocracy with Charlie Chaplin. Little Fairbanks said, "I have read almost all the books about Technocracy. In my opinion, it won't work. What's the reason? Because in my opinion, Technocracy is a utopian idea of averaging out humanity. I think this is impossible. This kind of ideal often sounds good on paper, but when it is put into practice, it won't work."

After a while, old Fairbanks also joined the discussion. He said, "My son knows more than I do. But I am an incurable optimist. Whether Technocracy works or not, the world will always improve. On a personal level, if this matter is beneficial to the public, I will of course support it." Charlie Chaplin said, "I have done in-depth research on the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan. Although Technocracy is a completely different ideal, in my opinion, it is not easy to succeed. But the rate at which the world is progressing now is very surprising. I firmly believe that in three years, there will be a new world and a new civilization. I hope that in the future, we will be able to live a utopian life like on the island of Bali in the South Pacific." Jack Oakie said, "What? What will happen to all the money I've saved for so many years? If Technocracy is implemented, there will be more and more fools in the world. The phrase 'diligent management' will completely lose its meaning. People don't have to struggle to improve." Lee Tracy heard this and immediately corrected him, saying, "Is money the only purpose of life? Indeed, money is extremely important, but you can't say that humans have no other ambitions besides money. Such as the ambition for fame..."

Carole Lombard was worried. She said, "After Technocracy is implemented, do women all have to wear the same clothes? I don't agree with that. I like to wear some unique clothes." A typist named Lucy also said, "Wow, 20,000 yuan a year is not bad. I support it!" A newsboy also shouted "Technocracy!" "I support it very much if I don't have to work until I'm 25 years old. A light bulb craftsman said, "As a light bulb craftsman, I first have to study electrical engineering for six years, and I only earn a few dollars a week. But he (referring to a star) hasn't even received much education, and he earns thousands of dollars a week. This is too unfair. Let experts handle this kind of thing, and it won't be so messed up."

However, a temporary actor who earns seven and a half dollars a day actually opposed it. He said, "I work hard and earn seven and a half dollars a day. But I have my future, and I work hard for that future. If everything is averaged out, I will lose my goal of striving. The meaning of my life will be reduced." (The End)

Audience Opinions

After Viewing "Innocence"

— Xu Hairong

The performance aspect starts off awkwardly. Why use a written explanation for something that happened eighteen years ago? This filming method makes it even harder for the audience to understand. For example, after Wei Guang is released from prison, it immediately cuts to Pipa returning home from the streets. If we hadn't read the synopsis beforehand, we would be completely lost. The two young women sitting behind me, during that scene, I heard them repeatedly asking each other, "Who is this? Who is this?" This clearly demonstrates the inappropriateness of such filming.

I found the actors' performances too reminiscent of the "civilized drama" style. Their movements don't seem very natural, especially Han Langan's portrayal of the dance hall manager, which is far too exaggerated and absurd, resulting in a lack of authenticity throughout. Shanghai Company's cinematography and set design are consistently high-quality, and they maintain that reputation in this film. Some of the shots are truly well-done, such as the seaside scenes, which evoke a nameless sense of beauty. The director also employs some clever techniques that can be considered successful, and the ending scene is extremely clever and worthy of praise.

After Viewing "Tiger Roar, Lion's Howl"

— Kun Ming

After the slapstick short, the feature film "Tiger Roar, Lion's Howl" starts with a bang. The entire film is very intense, especially the scenes of Clyde Beatty's training, and the scene of the fierce tiger and lion fight, with fur flying everywhere during the "Tiger Roar, Lion's Howl," is truly frightening. The comedic interludes are also well-integrated.

Although male lead Clyde Beatty performs under the intense gaze of angry tigers and lions, with danger imminent, his demeanor remains calm and composed. Female supporting actress Anita Dage, although a beautiful star, is unable to fully express her talent in this film, which buries her talent. In conclusion, this is worth watching, far superior to animal films like "Human and Animal Spectacle" and "Tarzan the Ape Man."

A Clear Song in "Vitality"

— Yun

In "Vitality," Chen Yumei very gently, filled with motherly love, coaxes her beloved child to sleep, singing a lullaby:

My little darling, darling, sleep quickly; sleep early at night, wake up early at dawn. Darling is so lovely, face like a rose. My good heart! Heart's little darling! Darling, close your eyes, heart, sleep quickly! Darling!

But her younger sister (played by Yuan Meiyun) also uses her melodious voice, not allowing her sister to monopolize the stage, singing a lively and happy song of butterflies and bees:

Butterfly, fly, fly, fly east, fly west, get lost in the flowers! Flowers as pillows, leaves as blankets, how happy, how carefree! Ah! When winter arrives, leaves fall, flowers wither, the butterfly loses its support, enduring the cold, enduring the hunger, how miserable!

Bee, buzz, buzz, fly west, fly east, working hard and diligently, preparing for times of need, building nests and making honey, busy with labor. Ah! When winter arrives, the wind is cold, the frost is thick, the bee lives comfortably in its nest, with plenty of food, warm and comfortable, endless happiness!

Talking About "New Year's Eve" Again

— Li Yuan

Talking about "New Year's Eve" now seems out of date! However, it left a very good impression on me, and not talking about it seems to let it down.

Having seen "Grand Hotel," I marveled at the magical power of Jin Yuanguo's money, which can expose the dangers of human hearts and the hardships of life in the short span of a day. However, after seeing Lianhua Company's "New Year's Eve," I am even more amazed at the rapid progress of our country's film industry. This film can indeed be compared to the "imported" "Grand Hotel."

The use of shots in "New Year's Eve" is truly commendable. For example, when the old man (Liu Jiqun) picks up the wallet, first joy, then suspicion—hesitation. At this moment, the clever director uses his (the old man's) back and forth, retreating and advancing footsteps to express it, coupled with appropriate lighting, which can very well grasp the audience's emotional tension. The telephone scenes in the film are well-interspersed. The best performance should be considered Liu Jiqun. He can express the several scenes of nervous mood and chaotic thoughts. If he can work hard, the future is limitless.

Han Langan has already given us a considerable understanding in "Morning in the Metropolis." In this film, there are very few opportunities to be on camera, but when the rich man (Xing Shaomei) throws the wine glass,

Mr. Han's surprise is very Chaplin-esque; sometimes it is even too much. If he can correct it, it is not difficult to be on par with Chaplin. I hope Mr. Han will encourage himself.

Talking About "Spring Water, Love Waves"

— Meng Gan

The domestic films after the so-called "change of style" in the film industry have indeed embarked on a vigorous path. Such as Lianhua's: "Three Modern Women," "City Nights," "Morning in the Metropolis"; Mingxing's "Torrent," "Rouge Market"; are all "good works after the change of style." And Mingxing Company especially paid attention to all women's issues, and this "Spring Water, Love Waves" is also a work discussing women's issues.

Here, it exposes the darkness of officialdom, the ferocity of the bourgeoisie, it put forward the slogan of going to the Northwest, and: gave those playboy sons who play with women a major warning, so this "Spring Water, Love Waves" is a masterpiece of Mingxing Company.

In terms of the director's skills, Zheng Zhengqiu felt that he had regressed a bit, because he was too negligent, but he still achieved considerable success in several scenes such as the lake tour.

In terms of the actors' expressions, Hu Die is the most natural and fitting, and she is successful. Yan Yuexian and Hu Ping are neither good nor bad. However, Sun Min has regressed much more than in "Future," and his expression is too stiff and forced. He is a promising young man, and I hope he will work hard! In short, this is an excellent and progressive work and is worth appreciating.

Hollywood Counterattacks Shaw

— You Ji

Shaw once said in New York: "Movies promote anarchy because they show heroes often using their fists to solve all disputes, rather than resorting to the law." Therefore, several Hollywood stars pretended to be brave and defended themselves, counterattacking Shaw.

"Mr. Shaw forgot that there are still people in the world who are willing to fight fairly," said Miss Kefulunxuesi. Miss Kai is a boxing fan, (not fond of boxing, but fond of watching boxing.) Also, actress James Jiana has done many funny things in films, he said to the famous playwright: "Only people who watch comedies would think of calling the police to solve those disputes."

The play is even more energetic in defending Hollywood, and returned a big cannon, hoping Shaw can hear it. In life, not everyone calls the police when they encounter difficulties."

Film Novel Maedchen in Uniform (8)

— Xin Fu

Produced by German Film Company, starring a joint cast of all female actors

Pei Bo walked through the hall and saw Mannila leaning against the wall alone, sobbing. Feeling a pang of sympathy, she walked over and said to her, "Don't cry. Wait for me in my room. I have something to say to you." Before long, Pei Bo entered the room and saw Mannila waiting there with a sad expression. They faced each other in silence for a while. Pei Bo was the first to speak, saying, "Man Fangla, do you know that they are preparing to expel you?"

Mannila then asked, "Then, will I still be able to see you?" Pei Bo hesitated for a moment, turned her face to the wall, and then replied, "Of course, I can't see you anymore!" Hearing this, Mannila's face turned pale instantly. She held her head in both hands and shouted, "Can't meet! How can I live on!"

Hearing Mannila's words, Pei Bo became anxious. She turned around and shouted very seriously, "Mannila, you should have confidence in yourself. You should be treated..." Mannila was already in tears, but she still tried to cheer up and asked Pei Bo, "Treated for what?" Pei Bo said, "Treat your infatuation." Mannila knew that she was finally disappointed! The future will no longer be bright! The person she loves most can no longer love her! She didn't say anything. She nodded, stood up, and ran out. After Mannila left the room, Pei Bo thought that something was wrong. She rushed out of the room and shouted, "Mannila!" Suddenly, she bumped into the principal at the door. She said to the principal angrily, "Do you want to know what I said to her? Come on!" So the principal and Pei Bo started arguing in the room. The principal said, "My school does not allow revolutionary ideas." Pei Bo said, "I quit. I can't bear to see this little girl unhappy all day long." But at this time, Mannila was like a lost soul, running to the highest floor, praying in her mouth: "God, heaven wouldn't be so dark, would it! I want to leave this world! I can't live on!" Poor Mannila, she had nothing in her heart except the thought of death.

In the dormitory, Mannila's classmates, because they didn't see her come back, searched everywhere, but where could they find her. Several classmates who were close to her started to cry. So the shouts of "Mannila" and "Mannila" and the sound of the alarm bell that people heard caused panic and chaos throughout the school. Finally, the classmates found Mannila, who was planning to climb down from that high level, and became even more horrified, shouting wildly. At this time, Pei Bo heard the shouts in the room, ran out in a hurry, and happened to see the students rescuing Mannila from danger. She was unconscious, sleeping in the arms of her classmates, unable to say a word. The students, seeing Pei Bo, surrounded her. Pei Bo couldn't help but gasp, saying, "It's good that the students saved Mannila's life, otherwise this tragedy would be forever imprinted in our minds!" At this time, the sacrosanct principal also seemed to realize something. She supported her cane, frowned, and walked down the stairs step by step. The whole scene was suddenly as silent as death. So this tragedy came to an end in the plaintive and mournful sound of the bell. (The End)
